  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_5ae97f53-28e2-4954-97c9-166138c0cb41'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

As Feyre navigates her first Winter Solstice as High Lady, s</span>
  <span id="freeText3547138098230234094" style="display:none"><i>Hope warms the coldest night.</i><br /><br />Feyre, Rhys, and their close-knit circle of friends are still busy rebuilding the Night Court and the vastly-changed world beyond. But Winter Solstice is finally near, and with it, a hard-earned reprieve. <br /><br />Yet even the festive atmosphere can't keep the shadows of the past from looming. As Feyre navigates her first Winter Solstice as High Lady, she finds that those dearest to her have more wounds than she anticipated--scars that will have far-reaching impact on the future of their Court.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3547138098230234094" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>

      $('span_class_gr-hyperlink_sort_order_span_tip_929').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

//]]>

<div id="review_2278502018" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2278502018" />
    <a title="Silvia " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13306676-silvia"><img alt="Silvia " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572029941p2/13306676.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2278502018?book_show_action=true">Apr 09, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Silvia " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Silvia " href="/user/show/13306676-silvia">Silvia </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13306676-silvia?shelf=multiple-povs">multiple-povs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13306676-silvia?shelf=disappointing">disappointing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13306676-silvia?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13306676-silvia?shelf=novella">novella</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13306676-silvia?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13306676-silvia?shelf=high-fantasy">high-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13306676-silvia?shelf=friendship">friendship</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13306676-silvia?shelf=best-squad">best-squad</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2278502018" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7416161930736548175">✨<b>Hardcore SJM fans need not engage, kindly move along without reading this review.</b>✨<br/><br/>Me after finishing the book:<br/><blockquote>IM FREEEEEE!!!!!!!! WORST EXPERIENCE OF MY FUCKING LIFE</blockquote><br/>So let’s start by saying <b>this book was <i>almost</i> entirely useless.</b> Things this book has:<br/><br/>• lots of walking around Velaris<br/>• shopping for presents<br/>• lots of bad innuendos<br/>• me physically rolling my eyes every two pages<br/>• way too much internal monologue about who had fucked whom, where and in which position<br/>• one really long and really cringy </span>
  <span id="freeText7416161930736548175" style="display:none">✨<b>Hardcore SJM fans need not engage, kindly move along without reading this review.</b>✨<br><br>Me after finishing the book:<br><blockquote>IM FREEEEEE!!!!!!!! WORST EXPERIENCE OF MY FUCKING LIFE</blockquote><br>So let’s start by saying <b>this book was <i>almost</i> entirely useless.</b> Things this book has:<br><br>• lots of walking around Velaris<br>• shopping for presents<br>• lots of bad innuendos<br>• me physically rolling my eyes every two pages<br>• way too much internal monologue about who had fucked whom, where and in which position<br>• one really long and really cringy sex scene<br>• <b>somehow galaxies were involved in the sex scene and that’s not even the weirdest thing that’s ever happened in a sjm sex scene</b><br>• mate mate mate mate mate m a t e ma te ma t e mat e m ate mAtE mATe MATE matE M a te <br>• "gentlemales"<br>• I repeat: <b>g e n t l e m a l e s</b><br>• a few cute moments<br>• a few funny moments<br>• <b>a tiny bit of actual fucking foundation for the next books</b><br><br>Basically <b>Feyre and Rhys need to retire</b> and let secondary characters finally have the spotlight.* The only POVs I genuinely enjoyed were Cassian’s and Nesta’s, which, surprise surprise, will be the focus of the next book. Fucking finally.<br><i>*except SJM has a talent for ruining main characters so what happens when secondary characters become the main ones? Uhhh we shall find out I guess.</i><br><br>Speaking more generally, <b>this book was just mostly bad.</b> I’m not only talking about <b>the writing</b>, which <b>needed a lot of editing</b>, but the general feeling surrounding it all. Starting from the blurb, which is just a few sentences from the first chapter copypasted together. People, the blurb doesn’t even make sense. That extra sentence about snow? It shouldn’t be there. They obviously needed one more sentence to make the blurb longer and didn’t know what else to pick. It’s just bad. Whoever did that did a very poor job.* And that makes me angry.<br><b>*EDIT: oh boy they changed the blurb!!! More than a full week after the book released! But I got receipts. #NeverForgetTheBlurb</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1525899005i/25513099._SY540_.jpg" width="500" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Authors, even big ones, still have to fight hard to see their books picked up by publishers, be sold, and then be read and hyped by readers. But apparently that rule doesn’t apply to SJM. <b>The publisher doesn’t even put any effort in pre-release things like writing a decent blurb</b>, because they know her books are going to sell anyway. And I mean, I’m here writing this review because I’ve read this book despite swearing that I was done with this series after ACOWAR, because she has a talent for making you want to know what happens to the characters, even if (especially if) they’re not the main ones.<br><br>But the least the author and the publisher could do is put some fucking effort and deliver a product that’s better than this. Instead, it feels like <b>either SJM is a rare case of writer who gets worse every book she writes, or the publisher has decided that she’s still going to sell regardless how many rounds of editing her books get,</b> so they might as well never edit them, thus never delivering a polished book.<br><br>Because, folks, we might have started making fun of the word <i>m*te</i> for shits and giggles, but it’s become a big fucking problem, especially in this book. You know the writing advice that says to just use someone’s name when talking about them, instead of saying, idk, “the French girl,” or “the red-haired boy”? SJM has never heard of it. Think about your own internal monologue. Do you think of your spouse as “my spouse” all the time? Or do you simply think about them with their name?<br><i>
  <blockquote>Cassian and my mate’s sister did not speak to each other at all.</blockquote>
</i><br>This sentence just does not flow. And it’s just one of about 70 times the word m*te was used (and keep in mind this is a 200 pages book). <b>I wonder how many creative writing students failed their assignments for doing exactly what the most hyped YA fantasy author these days does constantly.</b><br><b></b><br>Do we also want to have The Talk about the <b>weird connotations and implications</b> that this word has? Oh boy, this conversation is about three years late, but I absolutely Do Not like all this animalistic shit, starting with m*te, moving on to how many times people purr, referring to people as males and females (ah, the good ol’ binary) (YES I FUCKING KNOW SHE CAN’T CALL THEM MEN AND WOMEN BUT JFC JUST STOP), to the weird possessiveness that the whole m*ting system entails. Also!!! Toxic masculinity!!!!!!! Weird unchallenged sexist comments!!!!! Trying to make Rhys sound soooo feminist when apparently his job is being horny 24/7!!!!!! Have Rhys (a literal sexual abuse victim) talk about how he <u>can’t stand</u> to be next to his m*te without, and I quote, BEING BURIED INSIDE HER!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!! <br><br>Ohhhh now you've done it, you got me mad. If you read a SJM book it seems like thinking/talking/having sex for most part of your day is the normalcy. Which it can be!!!! But guess what! Ace people exist!!!! People with low sexual drive exist!!!!!!!!!! That’s normal too!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!! Oh no I’m using too many exclamation points let me hire an editor. When every single character you portray acts the same exact way towards something like sex, you’re telling your readers (mostly teens) that that’s what’s expected of them, that that’s how everyone is like. It’s no secret that diversity doesn’t exist in SJM’s world, and that involves how people view sex and romantic relationships too.<br><br>It’s amazing that YA books have sex positivity. <b>But books need to also acknowledge that ace people exist too. Protagonists and love interests that aren’t some sort of sex gods need to be there too. Thin boys, fat boys, trans boys need to be there too.</b> <u>
  <b>If after &gt;10 books a writer can’t get out of her own self-insert fantasies about what type of men she likes, maybe she isn’t a great writer after all.</b>
</u> Maybe she needs to listen to the (still too small) part of her readers that demand More, that demand Better.<br><br>I went on a HUGE tangent and I don't even fucking care. There were parts of the book that I liked. I even enjoyed most of its central part. I enjoyed Nesta’s PTSD portrayal and she’s the only reason I’m going to read the next book because parts of her trauma and her way of dealing with it have the potential to mean so fucking much to me. But I’m going to lower my rating to 1 star because I’m tired of all the things I mentioned above, <b>I'm tired of being treated like shit by an author and her team because they expect me to worship her when she doesn't even try anymore.</b> My 1 star isn't even gonna change anything because everyone’s giving this the usual five stars, but I don’t care. I’m here and as a reader <b>I demand better, I demand the bare fucking minimum</b>, and I don’t think this book even tried.<br><br><i>This was a buddy read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/23238315-rin-lorenzo" rel="nofollow noopener">my bon m@te</a> (I’m sorry)</i><br><br>____<br><br>Correct me if I'm wrong but shouldn't blurbs, like, tell you something about the book..........why is this one just a recap of the previous ones lmao<br><br><br>Also shout-out to sjm for managing to squeeze the word "mate" within like 100 words of bad blurb</span>
  <a data-text-id="7416161930736548175" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2093429105" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2093429105" />
    <a title="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries"><img alt="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557144778p2/15335689.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2093429105?book_show_action=true">Aug 15, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" class="user" itemprop="url" name="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" href="/user/show/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries">destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=fae">fae</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=found-families">found-families</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=otp">otp</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=owned-physical">owned-physical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2093429105" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer513711567724066990"><blockquote>#1 <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1836177157' rel='nofollow noopener'>A Court of Thorns and Roses</a> ★★★★★<br/>#2 <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1837779409' rel='nofollow noopener'>A Court of Mist and Fury</a> ★★★★★<br/>#3 <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1838516558' rel='nofollow noopener'>A Court of Wings and Ruin</a> ★★★★★<br/>#3.5 <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2093429105' rel='nofollow noopener'>A Court of Frost and Starlight</a> ★★★★★</blockquote><br/>First of all, let me just express my total devastation that an entire year of counting down the days until this book’s release is <i>gone</i> in two and a half hours of reading. I mean, I knew it was only going to be a novella, but… *sobs quietly* <i>I didn’t expect it to go by THAT fast!</i> This amazing little series has pulled me through some really dark times and </span>
  <span id="freeText513711567724066990" style="display:none"><blockquote>#1 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1836177157" rel="nofollow noopener">A Court of Thorns and Roses</a> ★★★★★<br />#2 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1837779409" rel="nofollow noopener">A Court of Mist and Fury</a> ★★★★★<br />#3 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1838516558" rel="nofollow noopener">A Court of Wings and Ruin</a> ★★★★★<br />#3.5 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2093429105" rel="nofollow noopener">A Court of Frost and Starlight</a> ★★★★★</blockquote><br />First of all, let me just express my total devastation that an entire year of counting down the days until this book’s release is <i>gone</i> in two and a half hours of reading. I mean, I knew it was only going to be a novella, but… *sobs quietly* <i>I didn’t expect it to go by THAT fast!</i> This amazing little series has pulled me through some really dark times and brought so much joy into my life that I know I will treasure it, always. ♥<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>Even now, with that bond again flowing between us like a river of star-flecked night, the echo of its vanishing lingered.</i>
</blockquote><br />ACOFAS definitely doesn’t read anything like the 3 main novels; the chapters switch perspectives occasionally, featuring POVs from Feyre, Rhysand, Cassian, and Morrigan. What struck me as particularly odd about this was the fact that Feyre and Rhysand’s chapters were in first-person, while Cassian and Morrigan’s were in third—a slightly jarring writing style, but nothing too detrimental.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>In his stare, I could have sworn galaxies swirled. In the shadows between his wings, the glorious depths of the night dwelled.</i>
</blockquote><br />We do get some really sweet and domestic Feysand moments, but I was actually surprised at how little time they actually spend together during the novella (and how little sex there is—who is this author and what did she do with Sarah?!). We did finally get the infamous wall scene! There are some incredibly sweet moments, at least a few scenes of Rhysand being his lovable cinnamon roll self, and a completely expected but adorable turn of events for their little family.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>Shadows different from anything my powers summoned, spoke to. Born in a lightless, airless prison meant to break him. Instead, he had learned its language.</i>
</blockquote><br />Feysand obsession aside, I loved how much time we got to spend with Cass and Az, learning more about their respective histories and how they’ve healed from the war. With Cassian’s perspectives especially, it felt like this was written to be a legitimate “bridge” between the ACOTAR series and whatever comes next, which I was honestly fond of, even if the next book’s focus on Cassian and Nesta does have me pretty nervous.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>Lucien had not come here to make amends during Solstice, I realized as Tamlin opened the door to the dark library. Lucien had come here out of pity. Mercy.</i>
</blockquote><br />Perhaps the most unexpected bits were the ones in which we visited Tamlin—with a novella this short, I honestly didn’t expect to see him at all, and certainly not in the state in which Rhysand found him. I never thought I would feel sorry for him, and I still think he’s a walking, talking garbage can, but I still couldn’t help being at least a little bit sad to see how far he’s fallen. I truly do hope that Sarah will write more about him in the future, because I can’t help but always feel that, no matter what a jerk he is, there’s something interesting about his potential as a character.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>Cassian set me down at last. “What’d you get me for Solstice?” I smacked his arm. “A heaping pile of shut the hell up.”</i>
</blockquote><br />Was ACOFAS everything I hoped and dreamed it would be? Honestly, no. This is more of a 4.5 rating, but you can believe that I did not hesitate to round up to 5 stars, because at the end of the day, I got to spend a few hundred pages with my precious bat babies, and watch this adorable little family interact and taunt and fuss and cry and laugh with one another, and that was all I really <i>needed</i> this novella to offer me. I have missed the inner court so damn much since ACOWAR ended, and it just felt SO GOOD to fall right back into this world for a little bit longer. ♥ <br /><br /><blockquote><b><u>Bonus list of tiny things that made me squeal:</u></b><br />→ the sauna scene<br />→ snowball fight traditions<br />→ more “the power of art” scenes<br />→ Morrigan reminiscing (ow, my heart)<br />→ Amren’s newfound jigsaw puzzle obsession<br />→ “Illyrian babies”<br />→ Rhys cooking Tamlin dinner, like… what even?<br />→ all the fuzzy scarves and winter holiday vibes<br />→ Amren receiving a million pieces of jewelry as always<br />→ Mor’s terrible taste in gifts<br />→ SHAMELESS reference to Cass’ wingspan</blockquote><br />You can find this review and more on my <a href="https://howlinglibraries.com/2018/05/01/a-court-of-frost-and-starlight/" rel="nofollow noopener">blog</a>, or you can follow me on <a href="https://twitter.com/howlinglibrary" rel="nofollow noopener">twitter</a>, <a href="https://instagram.com/howlinglibraries" rel="nofollow noopener">bookstagram</a>, or <a href="https://facebook.com/howlinglibraries" rel="nofollow noopener">facebook</a>!</span>
  <a data-text-id="513711567724066990" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2156153158" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2156153158" />
    <a title="Chelsea Humphrey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/47207032-chelsea-humphrey"><img alt="Chelsea Humphrey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585613513p2/47207032.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2156153158?book_show_action=true">Nov 15, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelsea Humphrey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelsea Humphrey" href="/user/show/47207032-chelsea-humphrey">Chelsea Humphrey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Chelsea by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/56660219-noelle-holmes">Noelle Holmes</a>
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2156153158" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5058009743368193614">Ok, it's time for an unpopular opinion. I'm sure I'll get nasty-grammed all the way until next year for this but..... <i>I didn't enjoy this. Not in the slightest. </i> Granted, this is all opinion based; there's nothing inherently wrong with this book, I just found myself bored from beginning to end. In fact, I felt like the chapter excerpt for book #4 in the back had more to offer than this entire "novella" provided in 220+ pages. If you loved this one, I truly am happy for you, but I felt the need t</span>
  <span id="freeText5058009743368193614" style="display:none">Ok, it's time for an unpopular opinion. I'm sure I'll get nasty-grammed all the way until next year for this but..... <i>I didn't enjoy this. Not in the slightest. </i> Granted, this is all opinion based; there's nothing inherently wrong with this book, I just found myself bored from beginning to end. In fact, I felt like the chapter excerpt for book #4 in the back had more to offer than this entire "novella" provided in 220+ pages. If you loved this one, I truly am happy for you, but I felt the need to provide some honest feedback in case there are others who may have the same expectations that I did here. I'm going to keep this as spoiler free as possible, but if you haven't read the previous books in the series I would stop here.<br /><br />********************<br /><br />I'm actually having trouble writing anything about the plot because nothing really happens in the story, aside from one decision that is made between Feyre and Rhysand. I did appreciate that the author was trying to offer a brief entrance back into the world she had created, and if this had been the beginning to a larger, 700+ page novel then I would have looked at this in a completely different light. I hate that I was expecting something to happen because it detracted from my ability to just enjoy being with these characters again as they shop for presents for each other and describe the food they are eating and recap everything we just read in the previous novel. But truly, if all you are looking for is atmosphere then you will likely enjoy this much more than I did. The descriptions of Velaris and the Illyrian war camps are breathtaking and exquisite. <br /><br />I did wholly appreciate the bit of backstory we get into Cassian initially, and my heart bled for Mor as she kept having to deal with her father and Eris and the Court of Nightmares, but every time I thought we were finally getting somewhere it would switch back over to shopping and food discussions. So I have to give credit to the fact that I was engaged in those moments, regardless of how the flow affected my absorption of the story. I was so disappointed in this disjointed lack of connection that I couldn't believe I was reading about the same inner circle I had once held so dear. <br /><br />Have I possible "outgrown" this series? I would hope not, because it's one of my favorite escapes, so I've come to the conclusion that a big factor is this: <b>I'm tired of Feyre and Rhysand.</b> It's not like I never want to hear about them, but I am so done with their narrative. It has come to the point where it feels repetitive and stale and dull and every single other character in this book, aside from a little bit of Cassian/Mor/Nesta was mostly left out. I wanted to hear more from all these other characters, from other courts spread across the continent, from <b>ANYTHING BUT FEYRE AND RHYS</b>.<br /><br />You know what I think the strongest point this novella has going for it? <i>SJM actually made me feel a bit of conflicted sorrow for Tam Tam.</i> I will never excuse abuse or the things he did wrong previously, but she managed to touch a tiny place inside my heart that wished for more for ole Tammy, that he could find someone to accept his brokenness and help heal him into a functioning member of fae society. <br /><br />I'm sorry as I'm completely aware that this review is just a bundle of disjointed thoughts (how's that for irony?), but it's the best I could do under the circumstances. Guys, I'll still read the next book, as I'm interested in the Nesta/Cassian deal, but I sincerely hope that we see more Elain/Lucien/Azriel, because I missed my precious babies. I really did. <i>Ok, NOW you can throw your pitchforks and knives at me, I'm done!</i> ;)</span>
  <a data-text-id="5058009743368193614" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2120481176" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2120481176" />
    <a title="Whitney Atkinson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14457130-whitney-atkinson"><img alt="Whitney Atkinson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1550868411p2/14457130.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2120481176?book_show_action=true">May 14, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Whitney Atkinson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Whitney Atkinson" href="/user/show/14457130-whitney-atkinson">Whitney Atkinson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14457130-whitney-atkinson?shelf=smutty">smutty</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14457130-whitney-atkinson?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14457130-whitney-atkinson?shelf=wheres-your-editor">wheres-your-editor</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2120481176" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14393408373368333250">we were all played like a violin in investing in this book. It’s $18 for lazy, messy fanfiction. This is 200+ pages of complete emptiness. There’s no purpose to any of this other than a money grab and longwinded, unnecessary epilogue to the original trilogy. <br/><br/>This literally reads like someone from Tumblr wanted a scene with all the ACOTAR characters having christmas together so sarah whipped out her laptop. There was no substance or set-up to a new series at all. 90% of this book—and I wish I was</span>
  <span id="freeText14393408373368333250" style="display:none">we were all played like a violin in investing in this book. It’s $18 for lazy, messy fanfiction. This is 200+ pages of complete emptiness. There’s no purpose to any of this other than a money grab and longwinded, unnecessary epilogue to the original trilogy. <br /><br />This literally reads like someone from Tumblr wanted a scene with all the ACOTAR characters having christmas together so sarah whipped out her laptop. There was no substance or set-up to a new series at all. 90% of this book—and I wish I was kidding—is just the characters all going shopping for each other's presents--multiple times. The other 10% is Feyre and Rhys speaking in each other’s heads through the bond about how much they want to fuck each other. Additional scenes include the characters getting drunk every 30 pages, weird side POVs from characters who add nothing to the story, and a snowball fight between warriors. I honest to God am not joking when I say if I read this on fanfiction.net, I would laugh at it and say it’s unrealistic and poorly done. It’s just pure stupidity and vapid smut for the fans’ wish fulfillment.<br /><br />The writing in this is so messy. “Gentlemales” brought me to a depth of hell I haven’t seen before, so thanks for that, Sarah. Every time a female character says something “softly, but not weakly,” I feel like plunging a knife into my chest. Take a shot every time Sarah’s written that into one of her books. The sex scenes have so much potential to be steamy or whatever but Sarah ruins it by having the characters CONSTANTLY horny for each other, so it dampens any tension or angst. And the amount of times that sex is referenced in Rhys’s POV is utterly repulsive. At one point he just <b>looks</b> at a table and is like “mmm I’d fuck Feyre on that” ... [john mulaney voice] FUCKING WHAT?? Even in Feyre’s POV when I could get away from his gross thoughts, he’d always talk shit to her down the bond and try and get in her pants or say something “sexy” but it’s just so corny and stupid and gross and it ruins the scene and I wanted to throw my book it was so irritating. <br /><br />I just think it’s funny how Feyre is the high lady and in Velaris, apparently women—oh, i’m sorry, FEMALES—are toootally equal to men *ahhem* males, and yet this entire book, Rhys is traveling to different courts and talking treaties and strategies with people and going off on business and Feyre does what? Cleans their home, goes shopping (no less than 4 times), cooks meals, and maybe if she’s feeling frisky, paints a little or has sex with her husband—oh, i’m sorry *ahhem* <i>mate</i> …. Sarah, don’t pretend that women are so equal to men but then literally only have female characters who love jewels and shopping and cooking and serving men and having sex. Even Amren didn’t slit a throat in this—she just complained about pooping and then had sex with Varian. Nesta and Lucien are the only vaguely interesting characters in this and I don’t like either of them. Their anger and distance made them more interesting than the characters in this getting shit-faced, making lame sexual jokes to each other, and referencing characters from the original trilogy I don’t care about.<br /><br />I wanted there to be something good about this because I genuinely loved ACOMAF and I’m waiting to feel a glimpse of the mastery that went into that book, but these new books just fan wish fulfillment at this point. This book was COMPLETELY unnecessary and the fact that Sarah is only extending the world to exploit the characters people like and get more money is just low. Let this series die, the world is done. The characters have exhausted their arcs and their humor is dumb and dry.<br /><br />Gave this book a star because Azriel deserves better than this bullshit.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14393408373368333250" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1891769620" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1158794002762398964"><i>"To family old and new. Let the Solstice festivities begin."</i><br/><br/>1) A court of thorns and roses ★★★★☆<br/>2) A court of mist and fury ★★★★★<br/>2) A court of wings and ruin ★★★★★<br/><br/><b>A perfect, fluffy and heart-warming novella, from the first to the last page.</b><br/><br/>A court of frost and starlight focuses once more on Feyre and Rhysand and I couldn't be happier about it. I know many people weren't happy about getting another book about them but they still hold a special place in my heart so <i>a new whole canon book about the</i></span>
  <span id="freeText1158794002762398964" style="display:none"><i>"To family old and new. Let the Solstice festivities begin."</i><br /><br />1) A court of thorns and roses ★★★★☆<br />2) A court of mist and fury ★★★★★<br />2) A court of wings and ruin ★★★★★<br /><br /><b>A perfect, fluffy and heart-warming novella, from the first to the last page.</b><br /><br />A court of frost and starlight focuses once more on Feyre and Rhysand and I couldn't be happier about it. I know many people weren't happy about getting another book about them but they still hold a special place in my heart so <i>a new whole canon book about them?</i> It felt like Christmas morning for me lol.<br />Besides that, from my point of view the book is more about <b>seeing the inner circle heal after the war</b> than feysand. Some dealt with it better than others but everyone has its own scars.<br /><br />I loved seeing <b>the progression of Feyre and Rhysand's relationship,</b> they're my all time favorite fictional couple and seeing them happy and making plans for the future was amazing, after everything they went through they deserve it and no one can convince me otherwise. Plus, it was good to see <i>old Rhys</i> coming back, he was kind of less funny and flirty in acowar (understandably).<br /><br />It's true,<b> the plot was basically non existent but I mean ... uhm what were you expecting?</b> I lost count of how many times Sarah said the whole book's purpose was giving a deserved ending to the feysand arc and creating a bridge between the two series. That's exactly what she did so I don't get the amount of hate I'm reading about this topic.<br /><br />Plus, the final excerpt confirmed that <b>the next book is gonna be nessian's</b> and I liked how Sarah set up the two of them (especially Nesta, her story arc in acofas is soooo dark). And I know that many people weren't happy with her arc but for me seeing her hitting rock bottom was the perfect set up for the next book, she has her own healing to go through (Cassian does too).</span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2278019429" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1899319719129822616"><b>RAISE YOUR HAND IF</b><br/><br/>you would rather read about Mor accepting herself entirely and unconditionally and growing comfortable in her sexuality; Nesta finding her way towards healing and self love and getting her revenge on the queens; Elain focusing on her personal growth and learning to healthily cope with being Fae and slowly getting used to her new found abilities.........instead of yet another uninspired, drab, unnecessary smut scene between Feyre and Rhysand<br/><br/>✋🏽<br/><br/><blockquote>✨ <a href='http://amzn.eu/9Jnbkf3' rel='nofollow noopener'>wishlist</a> ✨ <a href='https://runawaywithdreamthieves.wordpress.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>blog</a> ✨ <a href='https://twitter.com/kzabrekker' rel='nofollow noopener'>twitter</a> ✨ <a href='https://azqaban.tumblr.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>tumblr</a></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText1899319719129822616" style="display:none"><b>RAISE YOUR HAND IF</b><br /><br />you would rather read about Mor accepting herself entirely and unconditionally and growing comfortable in her sexuality; Nesta finding her way towards healing and self love and getting her revenge on the queens; Elain focusing on her personal growth and learning to healthily cope with being Fae and slowly getting used to her new found abilities.........instead of yet another uninspired, drab, unnecessary smut scene between Feyre and Rhysand<br /><br />✋🏽<br /><br /><blockquote>✨ <a href="http://amzn.eu/9Jnbkf3" rel="nofollow noopener">wishlist</a> ✨ <a href="https://runawaywithdreamthieves.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">blog</a> ✨ <a href="https://twitter.com/kzabrekker" rel="nofollow noopener">twitter</a> ✨ <a href="https://azqaban.tumblr.com" rel="nofollow noopener">tumblr</a> ✨</blockquote></span>

<div id="review_2093452655" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2093452655" />
    <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale"><img alt="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577855357p2/69106439.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2093452655?book_show_action=true">Jan 31, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale">Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781408890325" href="/book/show/36048256-a-court-of-frost-and-starlight">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale?shelf=faeries">faeries</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2093452655" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12876115095134254904"><i>”Mother above and Cauldron save me.”</i><br/><br/>Yep, that’s exactly what I thought when I read another one of Feyre and Rhy’s naughty scenes! The words might have been the same; my thoughts came with an eye roll instead of pleasure though. As did a lot of other things while I read this novella. Don’t get me wrong, I still enjoyed almost every second of this and it was really nice to spend some time with all those characters again BUT (yes, it’s a big but) there were a lot of things that didn’t sit well with</span>
  <span id="freeText12876115095134254904" style="display:none"><i>”Mother above and Cauldron save me.”</i><br><br>Yep, that’s exactly what I thought when I read another one of Feyre and Rhy’s naughty scenes! The words might have been the same; my thoughts came with an eye roll instead of pleasure though. As did a lot of other things while I read this novella. Don’t get me wrong, I still enjoyed almost every second of this and it was really nice to spend some time with all those characters again BUT (yes, it’s a big but) there were a lot of things that didn’t sit well with me and you can bet your lovely behind on the fact that I’m going to point them out later on when I get to the spoilery parts of this review.<br><br>Generally speaking this wasn’t bad. We got to see a little bit of our characters normal lives and I think we can all agree that after everything they went through they deserve some normalcy and happiness. It was nice to walk through Velaris, to go Solstice shopping with Mor and Feyre and to see those beloved characters interact with each other. They all survived the war and each and every single one of them is trying to cope with the aftermath. There are plenty of wounds that still need to heal and I’m kind of grateful Sarah decided to give her characters some room to come to terms with everything. So yes, this novella might not have a huge plot but definitely provides a good transition into the next series. ;-)<br><br>Still, there were quite a lot of interesting dialogues and a bunch of things that either made me happy or caused me to get angry. Mostly it was the relationships between the characters and so this is exactly what I’m going to write about. Buckle up! This is going to be a hard ride! *lol*<br><br><u>
  <b>From here on out, I’ll talk about the relationships and ships of the characters, so this isn’t only going to be rant and gush feast but also a spoiler celebration! If you still continue to read and haven’t read ACOFAS yet, it’s at your own risk! Don’t say I didn’t warn you! ;-)</b>
</u><br><br><b>The relationships &amp; ships:</b><br><br><u>Feyre &amp; Rhys:</u><br><br><i>”But you are bothering – you’re both still working to make this peace last. Peace, Rhys. We have peace, and the true kind. Enjoy it – enjoy each other. You paid the debt before it was ever a debt.”</i><br><br>I totally agree with Cassian and even though this might sound harsh now I still need to say it: I want them to enjoy each other too, but please not as the MCs of the following books. I love Feyre and Rhys, I really do, but I think from ACOWAR on out their character development was kind of detrimental. I already mentioned it in my review of ACOWAR and I’ll say it again Feyre’s and Rhys’s holier-than-thou attitude is beginning to get on my nerves. Feyre and her friends weren’t the only ones that suffered and it would be really nice if she’d get out of her pink bubble and would acknowledge the fact that others hurt too! It’s good that Rhys and her have each other but not everyone is as lucky as them and it would help to remember that they made mistakes too! Also if I read about “toes that curl” in Feyre’s boots one more time I’m going to be sick. Yes, we got it, Rhys is such a sexy male and they really love each other. If you ask me their story should have ended after ACOWAR because right now I have more negative feelings towards them than positive ones and this is actually kinda sad. &gt;_&lt; Okay, Feysand shippers are allowed to take out their pitchforks and torches now... Just give me a little head start, will you? ;-P<br><br><u>Feyre &amp; Lucien:</u><br><br><i>”And what, exactly, does this Band of Exiles plan to do? Host events? Organize party-planning committees?”<br>Lucien’s metal eye clicked faintly and narrowed. “You can be as much of an asshole as that mate of yours, you know that?”</i> <br><br>I think Feyre was a real bitch to Lucien in this book. And no, I’m not sorry for saying it out loud. After all someone has to do it and I don’t mind it being me. I mean if she really wants him to be friends with her, she has to accept that he has his own life and doesn’t want to depend on her and Rhys. If she’d be honest to herself she’d realize that Lucien isn’t welcome at her court and that he has his reasons to stay away from them. I think the only two people who feel real sympathy for Lucien are Az and Amren and they only do it to some extent. So yeah, she can’t expect him to be happy with the situation. Lucien lost so much over the centuries and now he even lost Tam and his second home. It’s not Feyre’s call to decide what’s best for him! Especially because she’s actually the reason why Lucien isn’t welcome at Tam’s place anymore. So nope, take care of your own court and leave Lucien be! Thank you very much! And a huge YAY for Lucien! Because he dared to call Feyre and Ryhs out on their bullsh*t and didn’t back down! That’s my man!!! &lt;333 Also I totally agree with him! Rhys shouldn’t have said what he did and the way he treated Tam cost him a lot of my sympathy.<br><br><i>”Your mate should have known better than to kick a downed male.”</i> <br><br><i>”I can’t stand to be in the same room as her for more than two minutes. I can’t stand to be in this court and have your mate pay for the very clothes on my back.”</i><br><br><u>Elain &amp; Lucien:</u><br><br><i>”He hadn’t mentioned Elain, or his proximity to her. Elaine had not asked him to stay, or to go. And whether she cared about the bruises on his face, she certainly hadn’t let on.”</i><br><br>So if you already put away your pitchforks and torches, guess now is the right time to draw them out again, because this isn’t going to be nice and tell you what: I actually don’t care! I’ll say it as it is: I HATE Elain! There, I said it! And I’m not even sorry for it! You think Nesta is a witch? Oh well, guess Elain is even worse because she hides it behind her super sweet appearance and gentle actions. By now I’ve reached a point where I despise her and I’m sick and tired of everyone defending this woman just because she is so sweet! Where was Elain when Feyre was taken by Tam? What did Elain do when Feyre went out hunting for them? Nesta might be a witch, and I can’t even believe I’m saying this, but at least she went looking for Feyre. What did Elain do? She got engaged to Grayson! YAY! Way to go! Also everyone loving precious and dear Elain! WTF?!!! Did Elain ever do anything except of looking lovely?! (Yes, she might be a great cook and good at gardening but seriously is that all!???!!!) AND WHY THE FREAKING HELL IS EVERYONE DEFENDING ELAIN WITH THE WORDS “Elain is Elain”!??? ARE YOU KIDDING ME!?? WHAT DOES THAT EVEN MEAN!!?? I’m sick and tired of her getting away with everything because she’s everybody’s darling! Lucien deserves so much better than that! She can’t even talk to him for a few minutes? She can’t even thank him for the present he got her? Where was her present for him?! And just for the record: LUCIEN DIDN’T WANT HER TO BE HIS MATE!!! He’s as innocent when it comes to their mating bond as Elain! It’s not his fault that they are mates and people better remember this when they judge him for trying to get to know her! She doesn’t even give him a chance to get to know her so she’s just cruel and mean in my eyes. If she doesn’t change her attitude in the next trilogy I’ll never ship her with anyone. Not even Az. No one! For all I care she can live with her precious flowers and become one of them! GRRRRRRR!!!! AKDFASDFJASLDFJKASDFLK! Okay, I’m fine now. XD<br><br><i>”Elain, at least, would be too polite to send Lucien away when he wanted to help. She was too polite to send him away on a normal day. She just ignored him or barely spoke to him until he got the hint and left.”</i><br><br><i>Those doe-brown eyes turned toward me. Sharper than I’d ever seen them. “And that entitles him to my time, my affections?”<br>“No.” I blinked. “But he is a good male.” Despite our harsh words. Despite this Band of Exiles bullshit. “He cares for you.”<br>“He doesn’t know me.”<br>“You don’t give him the chance to even try to do so.”</i><br><br><u>Cassian &amp; Nesta:</u><br><br><i>”A storm is going to hit in a few days. I’d like you to distribute this amongst those who might feel its impact the hardest.”</i><br><br>Cassian is so, so damn precious and he’s stuck with Nesta! That’s not fair! I think when it comes to me disliking characters in this series it’s a tie between Nesta and Elain. I just hate them both. (I know I’m making a lot of friends with this review. *lol* But I just can’t help it!) I don’t know if I’ll ever be able to ship them but after seeing that Nesta still didn’t change... Well, I just can’t ship them. By now I don’t even know if her character can be redeemed and if Sarah doesn’t work her magic with her I’ll never board this ship. And it will take a HUGE amount of magic to make her character at least a little bit more likable! And to everyone out there who likes Nesta and thinks I’m mean: I know she has PTSD too and I know that she suffers at least as much as all the other characters around her do, but that’s no reason to lash out at the others. If she wants to be secluded from them, live in a cheap apartment, drink all day and sleep with every fae male that comes her way: Okay! But to hurt the others, to fight them even though they are trying to help her, to spend Feyre’s and Rhys money without asking them: That’s not okay!! How many people have to offer her help until she accepts it? How often will she hurt poor Cassian because she’s just too proud to acknowledge that she has a serious problem? Just like Lucien, Cassian deserves so much better than her and I think I’ll make a petition for both of them! #FreeCassian&amp;LucienFromTheClutchesOfTheCruelArcheronSisters<br><br><i>”Nesta is Nesta. She does what she wants, even if it kills her sister. I’ve offered her job after job, and she refuses them all.”</i> <br><br><u>Tamlin &amp; Rhys:</u><br><br><i>Forgiveness could be a gift to both, but what he’d done... “Do you want her to?”<br>His green eyes were empty. “Do I deserve it?”<br>No. Never.<br>He must have read it on my face, because he asked, “Do you forgive me – for your mother and sister?”</i><br><br>I’m not okay with the way Rhys treated Tamlin! Yes, he made mistakes, yes he hurt Feyre, but that doesn’t mean that they have to hurt him too! Rhys should have known better than that, he should have been better than that and he shouldn’t have kicked Tam when he was already on the ground. Everyone can see that Tamlin is hurting and to treat him like that? To say what Rhys said to him? WOAH!! That was just cruel, mean and uncalled-for. I’m feeling really sorry for Tam now and Rhys helping him with the elk doesn’t make this any better. He only helped him because he might need him in future, not because he actually cared. Where is your compassion for Tam, Rhys? Where is the Rhys of ACOMAF I fell in love with? I don’t see him anymore. *shakes head*<br><br><i>”I hope you live the rest of your miserable life alone here. It’s a far more satisfying end than slaughtering you.”</i><br><br><u>Elain &amp; Az:</u><br><br><i>Cassian sat up, the portrait of outrage. “No?”<br>Azriel tucked in his wings. “Would you want people betting on you?”</i><br><br>I think the only reason Az reacted like that is because he might feel guilty for liking Elain. It’s so obvious that Sarah wants them to end up together and all those little tense moments between them speak volumes about her intentions. But as I said: I can’t ship Elain with anyone right now. Az is too sweet and gentle to end up with her and I really don’t want them to be together. Not because I would begrudge him a relationship with her, but because I think that he deserves better than her. After Mor played with him for centuries Az deserves the world, and then some! If Elain doesn’t change and acknowledges her misbehaviour against Lucien then I can’t ship this ship. And quite honestly, if I’d be Az I wouldn’t want to be with someone who treats their mate like that. <br><br><i>”Azriel emerged from the sitting room, a glass of wine in hand and wings tucked back to reveal his fine, yet simple black jacket and pants.<br>I felt, more than saw, my sister go still as he approached. Her throat bobbed.”</i><br><br><u>Rhys &amp; Lucien:</u><br><br><i>”I can let go of the taunts,” he said, scanning my face. “And the fact that he still harbors some hope of one day reuniting with Tamlin. But I cannot let go of how he treated you after Under the Mountain.”</i><br><br>I’m just glad that Lucien became friends with Vassa and Jurian because as I already mentioned above, he obviously isn’t welcome at the Night Court. Rhys still doesn’t like him and Lucien deserves more than to be tolerated. He deserves to be respected, to be loved and cherished and not to be treated like sh*t! Also what the hell does Rhys even mean with how he treated Feyre after Under the Mountain? Lucien did nothing wrong, he was there for her, tried to help her, defended her against Tam, spoke up for her and confronted Tamlin. And what did he get in return? Tamlin reprimanded him and might have even physically hurt him, Ianthe abused him and Tam let it happen because he refused to take part in the ritual, and Feyre?! Do I really have to point out what Feyre did? She lied to him, claimed that Rhys had turned her and even after she came back to the spring court she continued to lie to him and hurt him even more by destroying the only place he called home. Hell, she even used him to antagonize Tam and to destroy his friendship with Lucien. A great friend she was to him! And this after everything he did for her Under the Mountain. Hell, he even got whipped because he helped her and almost died as well. To destroy your friends’ life is a great way to show him gratitude. Well done, Feyre! So WHO EXACTLY TREATED WHOM LIKE SH*T AFTER UNDER THE MOUNTAIN, RHYS???!!!! Mhmm??? Care to enlighten me? And one more thing before I come to the end of this <s>rant</s> review: Lucien was in no position to help Feyre because he suffered from PTSD too. That’s something everyone always seems to forget. You can’t help someone else if you’re drowning yourself. And people better keep that in mind before they talk badly about him. <br><br><b>Conclusion:</b><br><br>I really thought I’d enjoy this novella and then move on to the next trilogy but for some reason those 229 pages kinda irked me. Big time. *lol* I guess that’s mostly due to the fact that all the things I already criticized in ACOWAR seemed to be even more prominent in this short story and I just couldn’t ignore it any longer. Also all the chapters we got from Mor’s POV didn’t contribute anything to the story, which is the main reason I didn’t even mention her in my review. All told this was a nice addition to the first trilogy and a good segue into the next one and I really hope that Sarah J. Maas will tackle all those issues I just pointed out. After all, “Hope dies last”! ;-P<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1517434348i/24976833.jpg" width="460" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>This fanart was made by: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://twitter.com/Niruskyart">https://twitter.com/Niruskyart</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="12876115095134254904" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2381195975" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2381195975" />
    <a title="Miranda Reads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads"><img alt="Miranda Reads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592243041p2/71848701.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2381195975?book_show_action=true">May 08, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Miranda Reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Miranda Reads" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads">Miranda Reads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=ya-series">ya-series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2381195975" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14412927308604545447"><i>*cue the undiluted screams of joy*</i><blockquote>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1526002496i/25520173._SY540_.jpg' width='300' height='300' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</blockquote> Okay. Okay. I will<b> <i>try</i></b> to be objective about this one but I just finished ACOWAR and I am still riding that emotional high. <br/><br/><b>
  <u>To summarize:</u>
</b> for a companion novel - not bad at all. It's full of <b> cotton-candy fluff, </b> and I devoured every single bite.<br/><br/>Now, this one was a bit <b>heavy on the smut</b> and a bit light on the Nessian but it definitely had <b>all the right feels </b>in all the right places.<blockquote>
  <i>Stars flickered around us, sweet darkness sweeping in. As if we were </i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText14412927308604545447" style="display:none"><i>*cue the undiluted screams of joy*</i><blockquote>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1526002496i/25520173._SY540_.jpg" width="300" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote> Okay. Okay. I will<b> <i>try</i></b> to be objective about this one but I just finished ACOWAR and I am still riding that emotional high. <br><br><b>
  <u>To summarize:</u>
</b> for a companion novel - not bad at all. It's full of <b> cotton-candy fluff, </b> and I devoured every single bite.<br><br>Now, this one was a bit <b>heavy on the smut</b> and a bit light on the Nessian but it definitely had <b>all the right feels </b>in all the right places.<blockquote>
  <i>Stars flickered around us, sweet darkness sweeping in. As if we were the only souls in a galaxy.</i>
</blockquote>For those who don't know (and are curious) this novel sprang from a<b> very drunk conversation </b> between Sarah J. Maas (aka the Maaster) and her publisher. <br><br>Maas confessed that in her free time that she wrote fanfiction of her work. Just little drabbles of what happened in between ACOWAR and her next novel. The publisher thought, <i>we could sell that...</i> <br><br><b>And thus, this novel was born.</b><br><br>So, keeping the origins in mind, <b>I really liked this novel. </b><br><br>There wasn't a big-bad or end-of-the-world subplot, not much plot development happened BUT this was a <b>fun and lighthearted</b> read. <br><br>And honestly, after ACOWAR, these characters <i>deserve</i> a few <s>months</s> years off from the doom-and-gloom. <blockquote>
  <i>“Dangerous words, Rhysand,” Amren warned, strutting through the door, nearly swallowed up by the enormous white fur coat she wore. Only her chin-length dark hair and solid silver eyes were visible above the collar. She looked— <br><br>“You look like an angry snowball,” Cassian said.</i>
</blockquote>Feyre and friends are spending their <b>first winter solstice </b>(aka Christmas without Christ) together. And despite the warmth of the hearth, not all of the winter chill is kept out.<br><br>Feyre frets about <b>reuniting her family.</b><br><br><b>Rhysand freaks </b>out about what to buy her (Solstice and birthday presents!!). <br><br>Mor is <b>absolutely terrible</b> at expressing her feelings (and gift-giving in general).<br><br>And Amren makes out <b>like a bandit </b>(mostly cause everyone knows what to buy her - priceless jewels).<br><br>And, of course, <b> Nesta being Nesta</b> made this novel shine. <br><br>Every time she and Cassian are in the same room the dynamic between them is just perfect.<blockquote>
  <i>He'd seen Nesta in that particular pose, too. He called it her I Will Slay My Enemies pose.<br><br>Cassian had named about two dozen poses for Nesta at this point. Ranging from I Will Eat Your Eyes for Breakfast to I Don't Want Cassian to Know I'm Reading Smut. The latter was his particular favorite.</i>
</blockquote> I know this is just a companion novel and that there won't be much development in terms of relationships but c'mon Sarah J. Maas. <b>Throw us a bone. </b>(Actually, if you read the sneak peek at book 4 included at the end, I suppose she does offer us a bit of relationship hints).<br><br> I am so <b>emotionally invested </b>in this series right now. I wish I could just time-machine myself into next year for book 4. But until I get that working, this companion novel will certainly tide me over.<br><br>P.s. I got to read the hand-stamped version of Sarah J. Maas's book. All I could think of the whole time was - <i>ohmygosh. She touched the book</i><blockquote>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1526000108i/25520051._SY540_.jpg" width="300" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote><br><a href="http://bit.ly/33ii2CT" rel="nofollow noopener">YouTube</a> | <a href="http://www.mirandareads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/miranda.reads/?hl=en" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/Miranda_Reads" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | Snapchat @miranda.reads <br><br>Happy Reading!</span>
  <a data-text-id="14412927308604545447" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2093533919" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2093533919" />
    <a title="Warda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30036082-warda"><img alt="Warda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593385153p2/30036082.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2093533919?book_show_action=true">Aug 15, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Warda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Warda" href="/user/show/30036082-warda">Warda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/36240535-a-court-of-frost-and-starlight">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30036082-warda?shelf=i-fell-in-love">i-fell-in-love</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2093533919" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5473560199561359322">Rereading this again filled me up with all kinds of warmth and goodness.<br/><br/>——————————-<br/><br/>That motherfuckin wall scene!<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1525207279ra/25466357.gif' width='320' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>Chapter 22 is officially my new favourite chapter after Chapter 55. <br/><br/>I mean, what are words at this point when it comes to Sarah J Maas's books?! She's my favourite author. Her books have brought about this sense of utter calm and happiness within me every time I read them. <br/><br/>This novella was everything we needed to potentially see the direction the other books will go in. And boy, am I </span>
  <span id="freeText5473560199561359322" style="display:none">Rereading this again filled me up with all kinds of warmth and goodness.<br><br>——————————-<br><br>That motherfuckin wall scene!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1525207279ra/25466357.gif" width="320" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Chapter 22 is officially my new favourite chapter after Chapter 55. <br><br>I mean, what are words at this point when it comes to Sarah J Maas's books?! She's my favourite author. Her books have brought about this sense of utter calm and happiness within me every time I read them. <br><br>This novella was everything we needed to potentially see the direction the other books will go in. And boy, am I beyond excited for it! (Understatement!)<br><br>I'm sure we'll be getting more of Cassian and Nesta in the next book and Sarah J Maas does character development ridiculously well and my god, being able to look forward and dream about their character exploration makes me want to pee in me pants, man!<br><br>I loved that we got see more of the Inner Circle. They are, hands down, my favourite bunch of fictional characters. I feel like I'm part of the family. I'm so glad some lighthearted, happy and sweet, tender moments were included in this. The family aspect between them all felt too real, and so good to read. And so worthy of them to have after the events of ACOWAR. <br><br>And the emphasis on art in this book and seeing Feyre getting back into it as a form of healing for herself and others was a dream.<br><br>The progression from ACOWAR to this felt natural and the cities and its people (including our main lot) were still healing, still too traumatised from the war. But progress was being made and I can't wait to see how that will be looked at in the upcoming spin-off series. <br><br>I think at this point people are more interested in the progression of other characters. I'm here for it, but I don't ever see myself tiring of Feyre and Rhys and the bond between them! Chapter 22 is all I'm going to say. After having lost so much, they better still have that puppy-love going. <br><br>I do think this aspect to the books that have become quite recurrent now, where some events have occurred and the readers haven't experienced it with the characters, is getting slightly redundant and I hope it doesn't happen as much in the other books, though this has become Sarah J Maas's style. In some ways that style can be and is ingenious (i.e. in ACOMAF) but I need more. It's not enough to be just told something has happened. I want to be there every step of the way for it. <br><br>Other than that, I loved it. I absolutely loved it!<br><br>------------------------------------<br><b>PRE-RELEASE RAMBLINGS!!</b><br><br>My body is ready! Has been ready since last year! No doubt that I'm kicking off May with this book. Which reminds me I need to take some time off work. 😏<br>Book commitments are the only type of commitments I do!<br><br><br>---------------------------------<br>[30/1/2018] COVER MOTHAFUCKIN PERFECTION. I AM DEAD! <br>BEST COVER! HANDS DOWN! <br><br><b>*flatlines*</b><br><br>[15/11/2017] <b>A COURT OF FROST AND STARLIGHT!</b> <br>I AM ON THE VERGE OF DYING WITH EXCITEMENT! IT IS SO DAMN BEAUTIFUL!<br><br>MAY 2018 WHERE YOU AT MAN?!<br><br>I just had a thought... WHAT IF IT IS FEYRE AND RHYS ON THE COVER?!!!!! <br><br>*DIES FOR REAL*<br>-----------------------------<br><br>WE HAVE A BLURB!!!! 😭😭😭<br><br>-------------------<br><br>MAY 2018 AND NARRATED BY THE ULTIMATE OTP, ME MA &amp; PA, FEYRE AND RHYS! GIMME! <br><br>SJM has mentioned this'll set the groundwork before we get to the other books. Fuckin excited man! 😍</span>
  <a data-text-id="5473560199561359322" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14391184750428755872"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1491959333ra/22467045.gif' width='400' height='300' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>One more time I want to warn readers, teachers and parents that this series isn't YOUNG ADULT. Distrust any booktuber, Goodreads reviewer/editor, and "prestigious" site that tells you otherwise. <br/><br/>If you are a teacher or librarian <b>Distrust the information on the genre and recommended age that comes from the publisher Bloomsburry Children's. Also distrust Kirkus reviews, Booktubers and book bloggers who say this is Young adult, Common sense media and The Goodreads choice awards for Young adult.</b> For</span>
  <span id="freeText14391184750428755872" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1491959333ra/22467045.gif" width="400" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>One more time I want to warn readers, teachers and parents that this series isn't YOUNG ADULT. Distrust any booktuber, Goodreads reviewer/editor, and "prestigious" site that tells you otherwise. <br><br>If you are a teacher or librarian <b>Distrust the information on the genre and recommended age that comes from the publisher Bloomsburry Children's. Also distrust Kirkus reviews, Booktubers and book bloggers who say this is Young adult, Common sense media and The Goodreads choice awards for Young adult.</b> For more on that scroll down to the italic letters.<br><br>THIS SERIES IS EROTIC/NEW ADULT NOT YOUNG ADULT. If reviewers tell you this series isn't new adult they're lying through their teeth. The result of those lies is that books with erotic content are currently labeled as CHILDREN'S BESTSELLERS or recommended to 12 YO readers.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1525664122i/25493735._SX540_.jpg" width="380" height="350" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1525664173i/25493766._SX540_.jpg" width="380" height="350" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1525664122i/25493734._SX540_.jpg" width="380" height="350" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1525664122i/25493736._SX540_.jpg" width="380" height="350" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1525664122i/25493733._SX540_.jpg" width="380" height="350" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>Is the author and publisher of this book really selling books with erotic/explicit content to young kids without warnings? Edit 10-23-2018. In the UK Maas books come with a warning <i>Contents mature content no suitable for younger readers</i><br><br>The UK Cover comes with a warning of mature content.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1539355777i/26439501._SY540_.png" width="" height="" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br> In the USA most copies of this series come with no warning of explicit content. I applaud writers that write erotic content, just don't sell it to young children. This is from Booktopia, an Australian retailer; It recommends the most erotic book of the series to readers AS YOUNG AS 12.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1525663699i/25493659._SX540_.jpg" width="380" height="350" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>UPDTE MAY 20TH JUNE 25th<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1529906412i/25852872.jpg" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Audible is recommending this book along with the first book of the series to 13 YO. However they are recommending <b>the most explicit book of the series to </b><a href="https://www.audible.com.au/pd/Young-Adults/A-Court-of-Mist-and-Fury-Audiobook/B01DYO0SZU?ref=a_pd_Young-_c5_lProduct_1_1&amp;pf_rd_p=a2025492-356e-4e9d-95f2-6bb0eaf5d9d5&amp;" rel="nofollow noopener">11-13 YO kids </a><br><br>That's why you shouldn't trust publishers to give the correct information on genre and recommended age in YA books.<br><br>**Don't trust MY review either**<br><br>**Do your own research and tell me why this series shouldn't be considered PARANORMAL EROTICA, PARANORMAL NEW ADULT, FANTASY ROMANCE or ADULT ROMANTIC FANTASY. **<br><br> You can start by finding out:<br><b>How old the main characters are? </b><br><br>I'll tell you, but don't believe me, find out for/by yourself.<br>The protagonist is 20-21 (like Anastasia Steel from fifty shades of grey)<br>Her sisters are even older<br>the rest of the cast is several hundreds year old<br>Isn't YA an age-based classification? Then why is this series labeled as a YA book?<br><br><b>How explicit the sex is</b><br><br>You can find that information on my <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1493972253" rel="nofollow noopener">A COURT OF MIST AND FURY REVIEW</a> updates. My ACOMAF review hasn't been censored by Goodreads employees yet as my <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2068533915" rel="nofollow noopener">TOWER OF DAWN</a>(another new adult book by this same author)review was. My Tower of dawn review has 273 likes so it should appear in the main page of reviews. Goodreads is hiding it. That sucks because it's the responsibility of parents (not of Goodreads, not of the publishers and authors) to find out about the content of the EXPENSIVE books they buy for their underage kids. But how are they going to find that information when so many booktubers, common sense media and Goodreads members are hiding it?<br><br>You can also find the information about the erotic content of this series on the american hardcover version of a court of mist and fury.<br>Pages 21, 22 <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[A faery woman is descriptively fingered by someone different than the hero, then she has descriptive sex, then oral, descriptions of the fluids and the nudity and the action in vivid detail.
