style="display: none">[A faery woman is fingered to orgasm by the hero (different guy from the pages 21-22), partial nudity, but this scene takes a quite few pages and it's an erotic scene, not just a sex scenes, but the purpose seems to be to be to turn on the reader. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>Pages 530, 531, 532, 533, the orgasm that shatters the mountains: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[a pair of lovers heroine and hero have sex including oral, vidid description of the action, use of the word "cock"  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>Pages 538 and 539 <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[vivid descrption of oral (fellatio):P but they call it licking LOL.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><b>DISCLAIMER AND TRIGGERS WARNINGS:</b><br><br>♣ IF YOU DON'T LIKE READING EROTIC/EXPLICIT CONTENT and don't tell me that you can skip the sex scenes, Most of us don't pay full hardcover price for skiping half the book ;) <br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[kidding, only A COURT OF MIST AND FURY book two is really erotica marketed as YA, the rest of the series is still explicit but not erotic <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>♣ IF YOU THINK YOUNG ADULT IS A GENRE THAT SHOULD REMAIN CLEAN<br><br>♣ IF YOU ARE 12-17 YO WHO DON'T LIKE TO READ EXPLICIT SEX SCENES<br><br>♣ IF YOU DON'T LIKE LOVE TRIANGLES And MULTIPLE MALE LOVE INTERESTS<br>Book 1 we have a love triangle: Tamlin vs Rhysand <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[(there was a third male who Feyre was sleeping with, but it was just a fuck buddy who was engaged to marry OW)&gt; winner: Tamlin  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br>Book 2 We have a love triangle: Rhysand vs. Tamlin but it's really uneven <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[for a while it seems as though another high lord might create a love geometry but didn't happen. EXPLICIT SEX SCENES of heroine with both love interests: winner Rhysand <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br>Book 3: NO LOVE TRIANGLE! <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Feyre and Rhys remain together, but there are other love triangles around and Rhys proposes a Male-Male-Female threesome to Feyre. Maybe he was joking, either way her reaction was unnecessarily enthusiastic for a woman who has already been sexually involved with 3 different men in the series and who is basically a newlywed. FeyRhys is still in their honeymoon period so why are they already joking about threesomes? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>♣ IF YOU DON'T LIKE ABUSIVE LOVE INTERESTS AND ABUSIVE WOMEN<br>-Tamlin love interest of book 1? ABUSIVE!<br>-Rhys, secondary love interest of book 1 and <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ primary love interest of books 2 and 3? Rhys tortured the heroine(there was a reason, though) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>ABUSIVE! <br>- The sisters? Everyone talks about how Tamlin should apologize. When will the sisters apologize? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Feyre's elder sisters let Feyre hunt for the family from a very early age, but they were always there reaping the benefits of Feyre's effort. When Feyre was going through an abusive relationship they kept receiving money from Feyre's abuser and didn't bother to find out how she was  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> ABUSIVE!<br><br>♣IF YOU DON'T LIKE WHEN sexual assault victims ARE THROWN UNDER THE BUS TO MOVE THE PLOT FORWARD. CAREFUL WITH DANGEROUS RAPE MESSAGES<br>It happens so much on New adult and adult literature (game of thrones, the girl with the dragon tatoo, the second book of the outlander series) a sexual assault victim gets the "oh-you-were-raped?- don't- bitch- about- it- and- move- forward treatment. So many books trivialize the worst aspect of PTSD and sexual assault and try to "sovle it" either with revenge or the magic romantic relationship that will make everything go away. Or the experiences just get ignored and brush aside! This happens to Mor, a secondary character in the 3rd book who is a rape survivor when <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ she's forced to work along with her attacker and the one who puts her through that was the hero of the story!  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>To be fair, I can understand the circumstances, doesn't mean I have to like that kind of story line, especially when that's something that good editing could have taken care of. That kind of disrespect for rape was unneccessary IMO. It didn't move the plot forward and it's out of character for Rhys to act like that. I love Rhys and didn't like the way SJM made him act.<br><br>♣ IF YOU BELIEVE ANY BOOK YOU PAY FOR SHOULD BE PROFESSIONALLY EDITED<br>I'm not a grammar nazi and my spelling is terrible, but I can tell you, even some fanfiction I've read has a more polished editing than this book. There's the overuse of words like mate. There are also problems with pace, repetitiveness, flow and consistency of the voices when changing from a narrator to the other and from a first person POV to a 3rd person POV. The characters sound too modern. The worldbuilding is not high fantasy at all. The setting of this series is pretty much like a modern series. All these are things that a content editor and a proofreader could have taken care off, but the publishers rushed publication lowering the quality of the editing and the writing. Even so they are selling this at full ebook price.<br><br>My ratings for the series so far<br><br>♣ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1272748928" rel="nofollow noopener">A Court of Thorns and Roses ACOTAR 3/5</a> because abusive relationships, false advertising (it's new adult dishonestly marketed as young adult) and love triangle. My review is currently censored and hidden from the third page of review. It should appear somewhere between page 2 and 3.<br>♣ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1493972253" rel="nofollow noopener">A COURT OF MIST AND FURY ACOMAF</a>4/5 because I didn't appreciate the explicit sex scene with OM, but I highly recommend this book to my friends who don't mind safety issues and like explicit scenes in slow-burn-romance. This book is EROTICA (according to the goodreads description of the genre) marketed as YA. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1509586350i/24339207.jpg" width="400" height="500" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>♣ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1637364378" rel="nofollow noopener">A COURT OF WINGS AND RUIN ACOWAR</a> 2.5/5 because poor editing, f bombs, repetitiveness, unnecessary sex scenes and dangerous messages. No, glorifying revenge and abusive women isn't female empowerment. No, in most marriage it isn't always the woman's choice, it's always the choice of both of them. My review is currently censored by goodreads.<br><br>Sources of my pictures:<br><br><a href="https://www.amazon.ca/gp/bestsellers/books/937688/ref=pd_zg_hrsr_books_1_3_last" rel="nofollow noopener">AMAZON CANADA CHILDREN'S BOOKS ADVENTURE</a><br><br><a href="https://www.amazon.ca/gp/bestsellers/books/937770/ref=pd_zg_hrsr_books_2_4_last" rel="nofollow noopener">AMAZON CANADA CHILDREN'S BOOKS FANTASY</a><br><br><a href="https://www.amazon.com.au/gp/bestsellers/digital-text/2524323051/ref=zg_b_bs_2524323051_1" rel="nofollow noopener">AMAZON AUSTRALIA CHILDREN'S BOOKS LOVE</a><br><br><a href="https://www.booktopia.com.au/a-court-of-mist-and-fury-sarah-j-maas/prod9781408857885.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Booktopia A COURT OF MIST AND FURY RECOMMENDED AGES</a><br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/genres/erotica" rel="nofollow noopener">EROTICA GENRE DEFINITION ACCORDING TO GOODREADS</a><br><br><a href="https://www.audible.com.au/pd/Young-Adults/A-Court-of-Mist-and-Fury-Audiobook/B01DYO0SZU?ref=a_pd_Young-_c5_lProduct_1_1&amp;pf_rd_p=a2025492-356e-4e9d-95f2-6bb0eaf5d9d5&amp;" rel="nofollow noopener">ACOMAF RECOMMENDED TO CHILDREN 11-13 on audible</a><br><br><b>WHY YOU SHOULDN'T TRUST BOOKTUBERS AND THE YA GOODREADS CHOICE AWARDS REGARDNG THE CONTENT OF THIS BOOK?</b><br>Because a vast majority of booktubers have failed so far to mention that this book series contains erotic/explicit content in their booktube reviews even though they always discuss "young adult books". It could be unintentionally. It could be intentionally. The reason doesn't matter. They're contributing to the false advertising.<br><br><i><b>A few</b> booktubers are being published or aspire to be published by the same IMPRINT of this new adult series. Others booktubers and bookbloggers seem to want good relationships with the publishing industry. They won't say anything that can hurt the marketing agenda of the big publishing houses. <b>Note: Bookables, Benji Alderson and Polandbananas have mentioned this series is new adult , so of course a lot of booktubers are somehow honest, it's not cool calling out an entire community of readers because the dishonesty of a few bad apples</b>. Distrust only the reviewers who call this series young adult. <br><br>On the other hand, The Goodreads choice awards editors ignored the shelving system when they selected the categories for the goodreads choice awards last year. In the goodreads feedback group they told me that's how editors select categories: based on shelving. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1525663133i/25493630._SX540_.jpg" width="350" height="290" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>At the time of the awards this series was shelved primarily as <b>fantasy and romance </b>by GR users, but still the editors made it compete on the young adult category. Not in romance (second most-shelved genre), not in fantasy (first most-shelved genre). They made it compete in young adult (third most-shelved genre followed closely by New adult)</i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1509590369i/24339479.jpg" width="350" height="290" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This review isn't meant to discouraging people from reading/buying the book. On the contrary. I'm inviting you to read this series if you don't have problems with sexual content and abusive relationships. <b>Despite all the problems I have with the false advertising I enjoyed the trilogy </b>. But again I'm warning you: <br><br>♣ NEVER trust the information that you see on Goodreads, Common sense media. and booktube. Not all reviewers are independent and unbiased. Do your research.<br><br>Life is too short and TBR piles are too big to just ignore the kind of information that can help us decide what we will read next. Goodreads shouldn't try to hide that information. <br><br>People who pay $15-18 for a hardcover and $8-15 for an ebook of a young adult "high fantas" book have every right to expect:<br><br>♣ 12-18 YO Main characters, <br>♣ no F bombs <br>♣ no explicit sex. <br>♣ A profesionally edited book.<br><br>That's not what any book of this series delivers.<br>Update 02-24<br>People aren't expecting something like this:<br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1527299376i/25598416.jpg" width="380" height="280" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  <br>
  <br>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1527299407i/25598417.jpg" width="380" height="280" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>For a series that is supposedly about women's choices, <b>when Goodreads, Booktubers and Publishers hide this information from young girls they are taking away their right to decide when or if they would read erotic content</b>. Not to mention they're contributing to the book being sold in the Children's section of multiple retailers.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_2093628018" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2093628018" />
    <a title="Melanie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie"><img alt="Melanie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577914102p2/3030788.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2093628018?book_show_action=true">Aug 15, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melanie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melanie" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie">Melanie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/36156268-a-court-of-frost-and-starlight">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=fae">fae</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=erotic-scenes">erotic-scenes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=signed">signed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=novellas-and-short-stories">novellas-and-short-stories</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2093628018" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1369507672676221925"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1525506843i/25484402._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>1.) <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1277792259' rel='nofollow noopener'>A Court of Thorns and Roses</a> ★★★★<br/>2.) <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1278845732' rel='nofollow noopener'>A Court of Mist and Fury</a> ★★★★★<br/>3.) <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1630234463' rel='nofollow noopener'>A Court of Wings and Ruin</a> ★★★<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“The first snow of winter had begun whipping through Velaris...”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><i>A Court of Frost and Starlight</i> starts out a few months after the events of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1630234463' rel='nofollow noopener'>A Court of Wings and Ruin</a>, and Feyre, Rhysand, and the Inner Circle are preparing for the Winter Solstice. The entire gang is also suffering in their own ways with the trauma they are enduring from the events of the war. <br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“But it had been </i></b></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText1369507672676221925" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1525506843i/25484402._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>1.) <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1277792259" rel="nofollow noopener">A Court of Thorns and Roses</a> ★★★★<br>2.) <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1278845732" rel="nofollow noopener">A Court of Mist and Fury</a> ★★★★★<br>3.) <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1630234463" rel="nofollow noopener">A Court of Wings and Ruin</a> ★★★<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“The first snow of winter had begun whipping through Velaris...”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><i>A Court of Frost and Starlight</i> starts out a few months after the events of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1630234463" rel="nofollow noopener">A Court of Wings and Ruin</a>, and Feyre, Rhysand, and the Inner Circle are preparing for the Winter Solstice. The entire gang is also suffering in their own ways with the trauma they are enduring from the events of the war. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“But it had been a long, brutal winter that had brought me so deep into the woods that day nearly two years ago. A long, brutal winter that had made me desperate enough to kill a wolf, that had eventually led me here—to this life, this … happiness.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>But there are so many lighthearted moments! Like, honestly, just picturing myself shopping for Winter Solstice during the first snow in Velaris? Talk about dream goals! And just in general, seeing this found family come together and be able to enjoy a holiday with one another after everything they’ve been through feels really nice. <br><br>My favorite thing about this story was easily the emphasis on the power of healing through art. This book beautifully showcases how important it can be to express your feelings through art, especially when you have no other means. This book truly is a love letter to artists everywhere, and it really meant a lot to me to see this topic be in the spotlight of this novella. Especially talking about the importance of kids learning to express themselves and giving them an outlet to do so, especially after trauma and/or dealing with depression. Seriously, the message was really touching and important. I only wish more schools took note. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“I have to create, or it was all for nothing. I have to create, or I will crumple up with despair and never leave my bed. I have to create because I have no other way of voicing this.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>My least favorite thing about this story is easily how it sort of feels like not a lot happens. I mean, this is a novella, and Sarah J Maas does gives us a lot of content inside of 224 pages, but at the same time I feel like a lot of that content is just about a group of people shopping for each other. Again, there are for sure important themes and discussions about trauma, loss, PTSD, and depression, but there is also a whole lot of fluff. <br><br><b>Trigger and content warnings</b> for some sexist comments (always contested), talk of loss of a loved one, talk of abuse, talk of past torture, talk of past abandonment, depression, alcoholism, and talk of war. <br><br>I for sure think that SJM also gave her fans a lot of what they were after. Like, she gave you all the wall sex scene you all constantly hounded her for. So all you little pervs can look forward to that. And there is a lot of sexual tension in general, even though there is only one (really long) sex scene. I love Feyre and Rhysand, and I’m so happy they got their happily ever after, but I’m just kind of sick of reading about them. How many times can Rysand smell Feyre’s heated core? How many times can Feyre want all the naughty, terrible things from Rhysand? At this point, it feels like SJM is beating the deadest of horses that have ever died. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Never enough. Not to paint him, know him. Eons would never be enough for all I wanted to do, see with him. For all I wanted to love him.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><i>ACOFAS</i> is mostly in the point of view of Feyre and Rhysand, but Cassian and Mor get points of view too, and even Nesta gets a mini one! And I know I sound a little negative about a few things, but I really did enjoy being back in this world for a little bit! And I absolutely cannot wait to see what comes next, with new main characters! <br><br><b>The rest of my review is going to contain <u>MAJOR SPOILERS</u> for both ACOTAR, ACOMAF, ACOWAR, and this book, ACOFAS! Please, do not proceed to read any further unless you have read this book and its predecessors or you wish to be spoiled!</b><br><br>I have done this in the past reviews I’ve written for this series, so I’d just like to break down each character and talk about the way they made me feel. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“I think my heart knew you were mine long before I ever realized it.””</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>➽ <u>
  <b>Feyre</b>
</u> - Okay, so her and Rhys are finally going to try to start a family. I was a little shook to remember that she turned 21 in this book, but to each their own. I have honestly thought Feyre was pregnant since the end of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1278845732" rel="nofollow noopener">A Court of Mist and Fury</a>, so I’m happy I no longer look as ridiculous. Also, I loved the selflessness of opening the art studio for kids in need. Again, best part of this story, hands down. <br><br>➽ <u>
  <b>Rhysand</b>
</u> - What is there really to say about Rhysand at this point? You’re either going to love him for his big heart and empathy, or you’re going to love him for his big wing-span and ability to knock pictures off the wall. Hell, maybe you’ll love him for both. <br><br>➽ <u>
  <b>Cassian</b>
</u> - Again, I’m so damn happy that he is going to be a part of the next story! He is such a kind soul, and I may have shed a few tears when he bought all those warm clothes, just to have the girl donate. He also always fights for women to be viewed as equal warriors to men, and I’m here for it, always. Best boy, and best boy deserves the next book.<br><br>➽ <u>
  <b>Azriel</b>
</u> - You all know I want Elain with Lucien, so unless SJM is really going to go there and give me a polyamorous relationship between these three, then I just get irritated that Azriel is messing with my ship. But honestly, Azriel is a stand-up guy, and a fun character to read about. But please, give me that polyamorous relationship! I would honestly commit a minor felony for it. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“She would rather die here, bleed out here. She would rather die and return—return as something wicked and cruel, and shred them all apart.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>➽ <u>
  <b>Morrigan/Mor</b>
</u> - Every time Mor has to go to the Hewn City, a piece of my heart dies. I love her, I love her so much. I want only good for her. And she is so much better than everything they made her endure. But anyways, the scene with her riding through the spooky, snowy woods at the end had me shook. I wish the entire book could have been about that journey and what was happening. Like, I loved it. Also, I was super let down that we didn’t get to see any glimpses of Viviane. Speaking of which, I really just want to celebrate Winter Solstice with the winter court, holy moly! <br><br>➽ <u>
  <b>Amren</b>
</u> - The chapter where she was talking about not caring about what body she took was a little weird for me. I am a cis woman so I’m not going to comment too hard on it, but I am very interested to see how trans reviewers will feel about what she said. But I’ll be honest, it did kind of make me raise an eyebrow. Like, please never say a sentence with “male form” and “be able to whip it out and go whenever” please. It just reads badly and feels gross. <br><br>➽ <u>
  <b>Elain</b>
</u> - And to touch on what I just said with Amren, the gross conversation made me think that maybe Elain was thinking about transitioning? And then I realized they mean back to a human, and that’s why I truly thought that the conversation was probably a really gross one that I wish wasn’t included in the book. But Elain as a character wasn’t bad or good, but it irritates me that she won’t even small talk with Lucien anymore. <br><br>➽ <u>
  <b>Nesta</b>
</u> - Nesta was damn awful this book. Like, hard to read about awful. And her going down this destructive path isn’t edgy or cute.<br><br>➽ <u>
  <b>Lucien</b>
</u> - My poor baby. My heart just bleeds for him. And him making sure Tamlin isn’t alone and is fed? Lucien is always the best friend to everyone. He deserves good things! SJM, give him good things! <br><br>➽ <u>
  <b>Tamlin</b>
</u> - Look, I’m never going to sit here and excuse abuse, ever. But I don’t hate Tamlin, I don’t. His parts in this book were the saddest and hardest to read. And he, without a doubt, had the best quote line in all of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1630234463" rel="nofollow noopener">A Court of Wings and Ruin</a>. I feel very torn about him, but I don’t want people to think I’m a abuse apologist or anything like that. But if she wrote a Tamlin spin-off, I’d buy it. <br><br>➽ <u>
  <b>Ressina</b>
</u> - My new favorite fae! Like, what do I have to do to get a book about her and her art studio(s)? Seriously, she had so many good moments in this novella, and I just want more. I love her! <br><br>➽ <u>
  <b>Eris</b>
</u> - Someone come end this man and everything about him. Please. I’m honestly begging. <br><br>Well, if you all saw my pre-review for <i>ACOFAS</i>, it was pretty much just me wishing that this book was starring Cassian and Nesta. Well, my prayers, wishes, and hopes have been answered, because the sneak peak in the back of the book shows both of these two being swept away on a mission in the Illyrian Mountains. The amount of excitement I have is something I can’t even put into words. <br><br>And I shed a few tears at a few things in this book, but they really came when Feyre had to go and bring up the damn Suriel. I swear to you all, the Suriel was my favorite in this series, but now I think I’m just going to cry over him in every book. But as always, he helps Feyre remember an important message that I wish more people would embrace in 2018. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“And from far away, as if it was carried on the cold wind, I heard the Suriel’s voice. Feyre Archeron, a request. Leave this world a better place than how you found it.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Overall, I’m not saying this was a perfect book, but I had a lot of fun with it. Yes, I’m totally sick of being with Feyre and Rhysand, too, but it was still nice seeing the Inner Circle, especially in winter time, and especially having snowball fights. Like, how precious. And I truly am excited for what is going to come next. (Also, I’m sorry if this review is a little all over the place! I inhale read for three plus hours and then wrote out this review at 3 AM! But hopefully you all enjoyed. Happy reading!)<br><br><a href="https://meltotheany.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/meltotheany/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.twitter.com/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://meltotheany.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UC4RbHEg_fH6CewJrh_0xJ9g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="http://www.twitch.tv/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitch</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="1369507672676221925" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2478633860" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2478633860" />
    <a title="Maria" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/77602709-maria"><img alt="Maria" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1519184646p2/77602709.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2478633860?book_show_action=true">Aug 01, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maria" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maria" href="/user/show/77602709-maria">Maria</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2478633860" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7278911092342261576"><b>3</b>/5 Stars ⭐️ ⭐️ ⭐️<br/><blockquote>“Stars flickered around us, sweet darkness sweeping in. As if we were the only souls in a galaxy.” </blockquote><br/><br/>I'm sorry. I'm so fucking sorry. <b>THIS BOOK FUCKING KILLED ME WITH BOREDOM</b>. I swear to God, I'm dead now. My ghost is writing this review. I'm fucking dead because this book had no point in even existing. This book isn't even filler. It's nothing. I can't even describe it. This book was SUPPOSED to be the bridge between the old series and the new series. But like??? This book was j</span>
  <span id="freeText7278911092342261576" style="display:none"><b>3</b>/5 Stars ⭐️ ⭐️ ⭐️<br /><blockquote>“Stars flickered around us, sweet darkness sweeping in. As if we were the only souls in a galaxy.” </blockquote><br /><br />I'm sorry. I'm so fucking sorry. <b>THIS BOOK FUCKING KILLED ME WITH BOREDOM</b>. I swear to God, I'm dead now. My ghost is writing this review. I'm fucking dead because this book had no point in even existing. This book isn't even filler. It's nothing. I can't even describe it. This book was SUPPOSED to be the bridge between the old series and the new series. But like??? This book was just messy archiveofourown.org fanfiction. And not a good one. Not one I would give kudos to or write a comment under. One I wouldn't read at all. But now let's go to the summary of the book, which is also inadequate.<br /><br /><i>Feyre, Rhys, and their close-knit circle of friends are still busy rebuilding the Night Court and the vastly-changed world beyond. But Winter Solstice is finally near, and with it, a hard-earned reprieve. <br /><br />Yet even the festive atmosphere can't keep the shadows of the past from looming. As Feyre navigates her first Winter Solstice as High Lady, she finds that those dearest to her have more wounds than she anticipated--scars that will have far-reaching impact on the future of their Court.</i><br /><br />See? Even the summary has nothing to prepare us for. As you all know, because I've been raving and raving about those books for a million years, this is the series which has reintroduced me to fantasy. This series holds a very special place in my heart and I have come to love <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3433047.Sarah_J__Maas" title="Sarah J. Maas" rel="nofollow noopener">Sarah J. Maas</a> as an author, too. This book was unlike anything she has written. This book was clearly a money grab, fanservice sort of fanfiction book. Which added almost nothing to this series. Everything that happened in this book could be included in a 30 page snippet at the beginning of the fourth book of the series, and it would all be ok. But let's talk specifics.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>The plot</u>
</b> Let's talk about the non-existent <b>PLOT</b>. This book was: shopping with Feyre, shopping with Mor, cooking with Elain, hardcore negotiations with Rhys, Az and Cassian, some good ol' fucking with good ol' Feyre and Rhys, and then again shopping, and then again some fucking, and some tension featuring Nesta, <b>ART</b> with Feyre, brooding with Tamlin, sexual tension with Cassian and Nesta, and let's not forget the epic new single.... <b>MATES</b>, included in the new album by <b>Feyre Archeron</b> and <b>Rhysand</b> (who still doesn't have a surname) <b>M.A.T.E.S.</b> (masturbation anal testicles ejaculation sex) (wtf was that). Let's be real here. Every time I read this fucking word I want to off myself. This word is ruined for me. I can never hear a dudebro call another dudebro "mate" and not remember this. Let this word rest. Let this word die. Let this word become <b>Frost and Starlight</b> (see what I did there). JUST LET THIS WORD GO. WE KNOW THEY'RE MATES THEY'RE MATED FOR LIFE THEY'LL BE TOGETHER FOREVER AND FOREVER NAH NAH NAH. Ugh. If I had one euro (yes I'm changing it from "if I had a dollar" if I had a fucking dollar I couldn't use it for anything) for every time the word "mate" is in this book, I would go to vacation to Santorini. It's expensive guys. You have no fucking clue how much. <br /><br /><b>
  <u>The POVs</u>
</b> This book added multiple perspectives of characters, which I found pretty interesting, but also unnecessary because nothing happens in this book and we don't need to see that nothing explained from multiple people, but you know, it happens. It confused me, though. We mostly see Feyre's and Rhys's POVs, in first person, and then we see some more characters' POVs like Cassian and Mor but... in third person. Which is really unsettling and baffling. And those chapters are such heartwreching and heartbreaking moments from their past, and in this book, it feels our of place. A book about the Winter Solstice which is basically Christmas, shopping, gifts exchanging, happy times, scenes like these seem unnecessary. I couldn't take them seriously, and I wanted to. Also, it seems like we're gonna get the next series with third person narration. Which is fine by me, but what's the point? <br /><br /><b>
  <u>The romance</u>
</b> I'm not a big fan of established and domestic relationships. Feyre and Rhysand literally murdered me in ACOMAF. The sexual tension, the eye fucking, the actual fucking, the "things" before the actual fucking, they made my little shipper heart die with happiness. And then... they became so canon, it hurts my soul. They don't interest me anymore. It's all sex and fucking and "oh mate, my mate" and "oh how much I love you my Feyre" and sky sex which was disturbing and like??? People can see you dude! You can fucking winnow and fly, just get her on a bed, or a wall (lol) or a sink or whatever floats your boat. I believe these characters's circle is over now. I'm truly excited for them to have a child but I guess we'll see everything from another people's POVs now. It's time now for <b>CASSIAN AND NESTA</b>. Oh man, how much I ship this. I'm so fucking board for this. They are my new Feyre and Rhys. I want this to happen so badly, I want to scream. Nesta pissed me off a lot in this book, but I will handle her for this ship. And because Cassian obviously loves her and I love Cassian with my entire soul. Furthermore, I don't know what to do with Elain, in terms of shipping. Az and Elain are cute af but I kinda want to explore the whole Elain and Lucien factor. Elain pisses me off, but I love Az and Lucien and I want to see them happy. <br /><br /><b>
  <u>Tamlin</u>
</b> This book made Tamlin an unnecessary villain. It's like this book didn't have a plot or anything or someone to blame shit on so just blame it all on Tamlin. Don't get me wrong, I fucking hate his guts. I appreciated what he did in ACOWAR, he kinda redeemed himself, but I still don't like him. Nonetheless, there is no point in what's happening to him. Everyone is casting him out. He doesn't have any friends, his home is a graveyard, his people hate him. And you know, he isn't the worst. We've seen worst villains redeem themselves. He's just a controlling and manipulative asshole who can't control his temper. He didn't hurt Feyre or Rhys. I want to see what will happen to his character, but Sarah has villainized him too much. <br /><br /><b>
  <u>The humor</u>
</b> This book was funny af. Hence my rating. The Amren peeing scene, the sauna scene, the "Illyrian babies" scene, the painting Rhys nude scene, the Feyre and Cassian drunkly decorating scene, the gifts exchange scene. It was all hilarious and fluffy and happy and it's something I needed. I have come to love these characters so much and I feel their inner circle as my home. I was truly happy to see them domestic and healing their wounds after the war. But, nonetheless, there was not a book needed for this. All these scenes could have been included in the fourth book. But, you know, money is important. <br /><br />Basically, this book was a character driven tease which gave us nothing! Honestly, we see things beginning and then we are given NOTHING. I want to know, I want to know everything. This book was diverse to anything Sarah has ever written. I was expecting this BOOM to happen but nothing. A big huge pile of shit and nothing. The book fourth snippet at the end was the most interesting part of this book. We kinda see what the next series is gonna be about. But still, not ENOUGH. Honestly, people, don't pay money for this book. It was too expensive for its size and importance. This is why I never read novellas and extra books to series. They mostly add nothing to the story. ANYWAY, till the next book in the A Court of Thorns and Roses series, which will be late af, K BYE!</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16507089318890888113">This is a great catch with the main heroes of the series. The last book was an all out epic, this one though a lot shorter is still filed with SJM’s great story telling and character development.<br/><br/>So far I have seen all these characters in the worst possible situations and facing incredible odds. Making great sacrifices and the legendary lengths they would go through to achieve their goals and protect those they love. Now when they have “won”, the work of rebuilding, forgiveness and moving on from</span>
  <span id="freeText16507089318890888113" style="display:none">This is a great catch with the main heroes of the series. The last book was an all out epic, this one though a lot shorter is still filed with SJM’s great story telling and character development.<br /><br />So far I have seen all these characters in the worst possible situations and facing incredible odds. Making great sacrifices and the legendary lengths they would go through to achieve their goals and protect those they love. Now when they have “won”, the work of rebuilding, forgiveness and moving on from the losses suffered.<br /><br />Yes there is no where near as much action in this book, and the characters are not moved along as much as I would have wanted but the are definitely important issues uncovered her that need to be explored later. This is more of “wet the appetite” for the next huge chapter, but almost as importantly a much need to assess where the characters are right now in themselves, and to each other.<br /><br />Though Feyre and Rhysand embrace their fate together. Others rebel against a fate they have not choosing with their very souls. This is the first steps in building a new world. A great point to catchup with everyone as they set their path for the future, to forget their past, or simply (stubbornly) deny fates chosen path.</span>

I didn't ask. i don't need to know that. who the fuck does. u already said that before. why<br><br><br><br>this was expectedly bad so yeah im giving it one star<br>yeah there were some nice things and it COULD'VE been more and i guess it MIGHT get better in the next books (because horny animals wouldn't be main characters anymore I guess) but i couldn't overlook annoying stuff so <br>im done.<br>im going to read catwoman and i wouldn't be reading sjm's books anymore if she doesn't hire a proper editor at least. [<b>update:</b> silvia is making me read the acotar 4. thats fair. i put her through this shes putting me through that. i hope it wouldnt be this bad but,,,]<br><br>anyway i buddy trashread it with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/13306676-silvia" rel="nofollow noopener">silvia</a> thanks for listening to me screaming and pls don't hate me for putting us through this<br><br>maybe ill add something here,, we'll see, im writing this right after finishing it so my patience is nowhere and my emotions rule me <br><br>~~~~~~<br><br>here we go<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1525118851i/25459505.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>br with one of my bon <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/13306676-silvia" rel="nofollow noopener">wives</a><br>~~~~~~~<br><br>why are maas novels' covers so bland and unoriginal when she's so popular dgdhjdfkls<br><br>will sjm be able to say dick at least once here <br><br>idek if I'll read it but i might 🤔</span>

<div id="review_2374753427" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2374753427" />
    <a title="Val ⚓️ Shameless Non-Snowflake ⚓️" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11626803-val-shameless-non-snowflake"><img alt="Val ⚓️ Shameless Non-Snowflake ⚓️" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605987751p2/11626803.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2374753427?book_show_action=true">May 06, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Val ⚓️ Shameless Non-Snowflake ⚓️" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Val ⚓️ Shameless Non-Snowflake ⚓️" href="/user/show/11626803-val-shameless-non-snowflake">Val ⚓️ Shameless Non-Snowflake ⚓️</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11626803-val-shameless-non-snowflake?shelf=3-stars">3-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11626803-val-shameless-non-snowflake?shelf=fated-mates">fated-mates</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11626803-val-shameless-non-snowflake?shelf=fairies-elves">fairies-elves</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11626803-val-shameless-non-snowflake?shelf=young-adult-new-adult">young-adult-new-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11626803-val-shameless-non-snowflake?shelf=0-in-my-library-read">0-in-my-library-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2374753427" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17553332552784747316"><b>3.5 Stars</b><br/><br/>So...I'm not in a reviewing mood at ALL; but I figured I better lay something down here before I completely forget any thoughts I have about this book and my experience reading it. <br/><br/>I had a hard time rating this.<br/><br/>Because, well, it just didn't blow my mind. <br/><br/><b>That said. <br/><br/>While I didn't love it...<br/>While I didn't really, really, really <i>like</i> it per se...<br/>I did <i>appreciate</i> it.<br/><br/>And here's why. </b> <br/><br/>Prior to receiving my copy in the mail and, obviously, reading the book, I received Maas' subscriber newslet</span>
  <span id="freeText17553332552784747316" style="display:none"><b>3.5 Stars</b><br><br>So...I'm not in a reviewing mood at ALL; but I figured I better lay something down here before I completely forget any thoughts I have about this book and my experience reading it. <br><br>I had a hard time rating this.<br><br>Because, well, it just didn't blow my mind. <br><br><b>That said. <br><br>While I didn't love it...<br>While I didn't really, really, really <i>like</i> it per se...<br>I did <i>appreciate</i> it.<br><br>And here's why. </b> <br><br>Prior to receiving my copy in the mail and, obviously, reading the book, I received Maas' subscriber newsletter email. In it she had the usual "woo hoo, it's release day" fodder they all send out, but it also contained - what I would later discover upon finishing the book - was exactly what was depicted in the "Acknowledgements" section. <br><br>In it, she talked about the process of writing this book and how hard it was because, in the midst of it, her father had a major health scare and almost died. Still, despite this trying time - she also found out she was pregnant - and, despite not really always "feelin' it," Maas trudged through the writing process because DEADLINE. <br><br>As someone who loves to write and also lost a parent in the past, I just really empathized with the creative struggle Maas probably had here. <br><br>Now, am I saying that an author's personal life issues should be taken into account when rating/reviewing or considering your own enjoyment of a book?<br><br>Hell no. <br>Of course not. <br>Absolutely not. <br><br>I'm just saying that, FOR ME, reading about that just changed the mindset I started the book with. <br><br>I went in knowing that, by her own admission, Maas struggled writing it.<br><br>So I guess you could say that 1) lowered my expectations bar, and 2) made me read the book knowing Maas had been experiencing personal pain while writing it. <br><br>And I think that emotion was definitely captured in the story.<br><br><b>This book will NOT blow your mind. <br>It does NOT really move the plot forward.<br><br>But what it did do, in my opinion, was move the CHARACTERS forward. </b><br><br>It really drilled down into a lot of their inner thoughts and longstanding issues and baggage and - as someone who loves character driven stories - I really enjoyed that aspect of the book. <br><br>Also, I mentioned this in a status update while reading, but for some reason, I am REALLY intrigued by Nesta's character. <br><br>She was totally selfish in book one and has continued to be heinously bitchy throughout the series, but there is just something about her strength, stubbornness, and just plain fucking resolve that I love. For whatever reason, I am just sometimes drawn to complex, fucked up, misunderstood female characters that everyone else hates. And I can't WAIT for the next book. <br><br>In fact, I think the character development done in this book is going to act as a veritable buttress to the next books in the series and make them even better for its existence, as meh as it might have been plot/action-wise. <br><br>So yeah, I guess I had more to say than I thought. LOL Oh well. <br><br>Toodles!<br><br>P.S. I thought I'd share the cool exclusive edition ends papers for anyone who hasn't seen them...<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1525638965i/25492122._SY540_.jpg" width="496" height="618" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1525638965i/25492123._SX540_.jpg" width="496" height="372" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1525638965i/25492124._SX540_.jpg" width="496" height="372" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="17553332552784747316" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9488552994614743583">If I ever, ever have to scrape my eyes over another bloated grody sex scene between Feyre and Rhysand, I'll just save SJM a job and poke knitting needles through my corneas. But it's not like that was the worst part! Oh, no!<br/><br/>Here's a quick blow-by-blow of this book's very worst offences: <br/><br/>- Rhysand is a "feminist" if "feminist" means "treat my wife like an orgasm dispenser"<br/>- the Night Court back at it again on their high horse <br/>- Tamlin's growth at the end of ACOWAR has been sucked away to the sept</span>
  <span id="freeText9488552994614743583" style="display:none">If I ever, ever have to scrape my eyes over another bloated grody sex scene between Feyre and Rhysand, I'll just save SJM a job and poke knitting needles through my corneas. But it's not like that was the worst part! Oh, no!<br /><br />Here's a quick blow-by-blow of this book's very worst offences: <br /><br />- Rhysand is a "feminist" if "feminist" means "treat my wife like an orgasm dispenser"<br />- the Night Court back at it again on their high horse <br />- Tamlin's growth at the end of ACOWAR has been sucked away to the septic tank<br />- Rhysand, a man who has gleefully carried out acts of torture and who encourages his military commanders to torture POWs, goes to chap at Tamlin's house to do nothing other than rub his face in the events of the trilogy<br />- he's a grotesque hypocrite <br />- anyone, ever, who tries to justify torture is morally bankrupt and it doesn't matter if he gave his wife lots of nice pep talks<br />- he is a fucking torturer <br />- and can we stop handwaving all of these characters' "noble grudges"<br />- stop kicking people when they're already down and we've already made our point <br />- Tamlin has been punished enough<br />- let it go and grow the fuck up<br />- also we were fine with Feyre's PTSD because hers was beautiful and sad, but of course someone like Nesta who grieves <i>inconveniently</i> deserves nothing but scorn????<br />- Nesta deserves better than these arseholes <br />- I'm glad she's taking Rhysand's money and wasting it<br />- I'm glad she's Moved On from these fake hoes <br />- Amren is ruined<br />- nothing fucking happened in this book<br />- N O T H I N G<br /><br />This is a PSA: the Night Court can choke. Every last one of them. The magic and romance of ACOMAF has been exorcised away and all that's left is 200 pages of shopping and heteronormativity. The only character in this whole series who was halfway decent was Tarquin and of course he was cheated and lied to and treated like garbage by that fucking MELT Rhysand and his Shit Squad who do nothing all day but shop and bake bread and cry about their sad love lives and then dabble in some more fuCking TORTURE.<br /><br />My goD JUST DON'T TALK TO ME ABOUT THIS UNTIL I HAVE CALMED DOWN.</span>

<div id="review_2117854563" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2117854563" />
    <a title="Nasom" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/67824881-nasom"><img alt="Nasom" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1520213174p2/67824881.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2117854563?book_show_action=true">Apr 17, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nasom" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nasom" href="/user/show/67824881-nasom">Nasom</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67824881-nasom?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2117854563" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15680802284189259901"><b> Real Rating: 2.5 </b><br/><br/>This book made me realize that I am more interested in the characters that are not in the inner circle like Lucien, Tamlin, Viviane, Kallias and even Eris (I’m really intrigued by him). Anytime those people were mentioned, my interest in the book rose. Unfortunately, since they are indeed not part of the inner circle, their presence in this was either non-existent or minuscule. <br/><br/>This book was said to bridge the gap between what happened in previous books and the next ones. I som</span>
  <span id="freeText15680802284189259901" style="display:none"><b> Real Rating: 2.5 </b><br /><br />This book made me realize that I am more interested in the characters that are not in the inner circle like Lucien, Tamlin, Viviane, Kallias and even Eris (I’m really intrigued by him). Anytime those people were mentioned, my interest in the book rose. Unfortunately, since they are indeed not part of the inner circle, their presence in this was either non-existent or minuscule. <br /><br />This book was said to bridge the gap between what happened in previous books and the next ones. I somewhat agree that there is a sense of direction as to what the next book is going to be about but most of what happened in this had no bearing on that. Honestly, I believe this novella wasn’t necessary and SJM should have written a full book. This book had so many unnecessary fillers.<br /><br /><b> What to expect </b><br />- Feyre shopping<br />- Feyre and Rhysand having dirty thoughts about themselves all the time/doing dirty things to themselves. The sex scenes/thoughts in this series used to give me anxiety because I did not want to read about that but in this, it was just annoying and old<br />- Feyre painting<br />- Feyre being sad that she was rich<br />- Rhysand being ‘perfect’<br />- To mix things up: Illyrian drama, Tamlin being sad, Nesta being annoying.<br /><br /><b>Things I liked </b><br />- My kind, loyal Lucien: I loved reading about him (mostly from other people talking about him) and I loved his brief appearance.<br />- I liked reading about Tamlin even though it was mostly depressing. I have a feeling his situation is going to change soon.<br />- I think among the inner circle, Azriel is my favourite and I loved reading about him. I’m curious about his shadows. <br />- I like Eris… I don’t know why, I tried not to but I can’t help it. I think there is more to him than meets the eye. <br />- I liked Feyre when she was not with/thinking about Rhysand. She’s actually a really nice and caring person. <br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Now to get to some details <br />- I know ACOTAR was beauty and the beast retelling but Tamlin in this gave me 'pre-belle' beast vibe with how lonely and depressing him and his court is. So hopefully, his belle would come soon 💕<br />- I honestly don’t think Feyre did that much damage in the spring court to warrant the current state<br />- I used the ship Nesta with Cassian like most people do but while reading this, I realized that I only shipped them because of the tension they have together. I used to like Nesta because I found her intriguing but she was so annoying in this and I honestly don’t know why Cassian still likes her. He deserves better and I honestly started shipping him with that girl at the shop smh <br />- I also used to Ship Elain with Lucien but she’s so rude to him. No one is saying you have to be with him but at least be nice. He also deserves better<br />- I don’t ship Azriel with Elain because their relationship gives me family vibe and not romantic. Especially with the comment about his mother<br />- I still can’t believe Mor hasn’t told Azriel the truth..Until she does that, I don’t think I can like her. <br />- I’m tired of being sad for Lucien. I really hope in the next books, we see him being happy  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Overall, if you’re a Feysand fan, you’ll probably really like this but I’m not so it was eh. <br /><br />This book wasn't worth my excitement and not just because Lucien was there for like 2 pages <br /><br /><b> P.S </b> are we ever going to know how rhysand became the most powerful high lord in history? or at least how that was proven <br /><br /><b> Pre-reading </b><br />This comes in exactly 2 weeks. I get to read about Lucien in 2 weeks (HOPEFULLY) 😭😭😭😭💕💕💕❤️❤️❤️❤️❤️❤️❤️❤️</span>
  <a data-text-id="15680802284189259901" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2093518287" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2093518287" />
    <a title="Lior" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/66261781-lior"><img alt="Lior" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1543889194p2/66261781.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2093518287?book_show_action=true">Nov 14, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lior" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lior" href="/user/show/66261781-lior">Lior</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer2093518287&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2093518287" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4580659548657322518">First, technically speaking, why was this book necessary? What was the plot? <i>Was there</i> even a plot? SJM said this novella is a bridge between Feysand’s story and the next story in this world, but what exactly did it bridge? <b>All I got from this book is anger and a gag reflex.</b><br/><br/><br/>If you’ve seen my ratings, updates, or followed me at all on here, you know I was <i>obsessed</i> with ACOMAF. It was all I talked about for about a year, from the moment I read it. <br/>I basically hated the other two books, but I loved</span>
  <span id="freeText4580659548657322518" style="display:none">First, technically speaking, why was this book necessary? What was the plot? <i>Was there</i> even a plot? SJM said this novella is a bridge between Feysand’s story and the next story in this world, but what exactly did it bridge? <b>All I got from this book is anger and a gag reflex.</b><br /><br /><br />If you’ve seen my ratings, updates, or followed me at all on here, you know I was <i>obsessed</i> with ACOMAF. It was all I talked about for about a year, from the moment I read it. <br />I basically hated the other two books, but I loved the second one, and got so attached to feysand. <br /><br />But, good god, it is just <i>not possible</i> that the person who wrote ACOMAF is the same one who wrote ACOWAR&amp;ACOFAS. (Yes I’m hinting at a conspiracy theory). <br />Like, ACOWAR was bad, but I still had some attachments to Feysand, even though Rhys was kind of a douche even then. <br />But this? This was <i>bad.</i> let me just say <b>this book is not a fantasy book. It’s a contemporary set in a different world. no fantastic elements other than flying (and even that was only mentioned for the purpose of a sex scene) were present in this book.</b> Feyre didn’t use her powers even once. You’d think she’d use this time to practice and perfect her abilities, but no. She might as well be human. <br /><br />But <b>what annoyed me most about this book (and ACOWAR too tbh) is the complete regression of the characters.</b> Feyre went back to roaming around the house doing nothing all day, Mor is <i>still</i> hiding herself for no apparent reason— homophobia is not even a thing in this world and even if it were we all know the Inner Circle would accept her no matter what, so what’s the point?, Nesta went back to her old self (though I kind of get that), Amren lost all her strength and fierceness and just sits around doing jigsaw puzzles, and Rhys, oh god, Rhys. HOW IN THE WORLD is this sleazy, sex crazed douchebag supposed to be the same loving, caring, supportive Rhysand from ACOMAF? He couldn’t go <i>two sentences</i> without making some unnecessary innuendos, talking about how good Feyre feels, how he can’t stand being around her without fucking her or how he dicked her in the sky while flying (???). <i>
  <b>His entire first chapter in this was him sulking and whining because he doesn’t get to fuck Feyre daily.</b>
</i><br /><br />*insert the world’s smallest violin*<br /><br /><b>But putting that aside, let’s talk about how “”feminist”” he is.</b><br />(I just wanna note that I know I still loved Rhys (less, but still loved him) after ACOWAR even though all those issues were present there too. It was just a little more subtle and I was still on that Feysand rush since I’d read ACOMAF only a month before. Now enough time has passed and ACOFAS has really solidified Rhys’ problematic behavior in my mind and I can see it for what it truly is.)<br /><br />In ACOMAF, he said [about Feyre] <i>”My equal in every way; she would wear my crown, sit on a throne beside mine. <b>Never sidelined, never designated to breeding and parties and child-rearing.</b> My queen.”</i> (page 621). <br /><br />And what do you know, in ACOFAS she is <i>constantly</i> sidelined, <i>and</i> trying for a child. <br />In fact, the beginning of this book <i>really</i> parallels the beginning of ACOMAF. I mean, yeah, Feyre’s in a better mental state for sure, but she still sits around the house being bored, or painting, or designing a house, while Rhysand is out there dealing with all the politics. Direct quotes from the book-<br /><br /><i>”perhaps I’d use the day to organize things. Find room for everything.“ <br /><br />“High Lady of the Night Court, Defender of the Rainbow and the … Desk.”<br /><br />[Rhys walks in while Feyre’s in bed] “Right where I left you”... “Isn’t it all I’m good for?”</i><br /><br />Like, are you fucking kidding me? Yeah, you crowned her High Lady, but the reality is that you never involve her in anything big. You just have her clean and do some paperwork. She’s a housewife. That’s <i>soooo</i> feminist of you! High Lord of the Feminist Court!<br /><br />Basically, <b>Sarah J Maas made Rhys such a supporter of women in ACOMAF to make the difference between Tamlin and him even clearer, and once we all switched to Rhys’ side she figured she could just drop the act.</b> Well, I got some news for you Sarah. It doesn’t work that way. Your readers aren’t dumb. <br /><br />And also, can we talk about the whole period thing? It was really cool to see such an open discussion about it in a book (no sarcasm this time) but... the idea that it makes women completely incompetent? Not so much. And that cheesy scene of him stroking her hair while she’s in pain? I almost puked.<br /><br />Oh and for god’s sake don’t get me started on the sisters!!!<br /><br />First of all- Leave! Nesta! Alone! <br />She’s been traumatized, and she doesn’t wanna be around the Inner Circle because it’s a constant reminder of what she’d gone through. Feyre of all people should know what that feels like. But no, she keeps pressuring her and practically blackmailing her so she would come. <br />And Cassian chasing her down her street even though she asked him to leave her alone multiple times. <br /><b>These people can’t respect a woman’s simple request for privacy. but hey, they have a High Lady! Yay Feminism!</b><br /><br />And I am just disgusted by how Elain is treated in this book. <b>She is constantly pressured by Feyre to give Lucien a chance even though she repeatedly and explicitly says she’s not interested. But Feyre doesn’t let up because he’s a “good male”.</b> Again, Feyre is such a feminist Icon!<br /><br /> Not to mention how much Elain is belittled and ridiculed in this. She may be naive, but she’s not dumb! she’s not a child! They all (excluding Azriel, the only pure soul in this mess) keep treating and speaking to her like she’s a four year old!!! <br /><br />I have more thoughts but I’m so angry that I can’t even make them into a coherent sentence and this is getting too long anyway, so the bottom line is, I only care about Azriel now, but even if there’s a book about him, count me out because I’m done. I’m just done with Sarah J. Maas books.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4580659548657322518" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2214381018" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2214381018" />
    <a title="Jessica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3283298-jessica"><img alt="Jessica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572125481p2/3283298.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2214381018?book_show_action=true">Jan 29, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica" href="/user/show/3283298-jessica">Jessica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2214381018" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer265050031013342532"><b><br/>ACOBAR - A Court of Boredom and Repetition</b><br/><br/>Yep, that’s what I’m going with.<br/><br/>2.5 stars<br/><br/>This was...painful. Painful, because I’ve been SO obsessed with this series and beyond excited for this novella and somehow I just ended up feeling immensely bored and underwhelmed. Sure, seeing those characters again was nice and there were some cute scenes but half of what happened in this book was a repetition of past events. You might say, what did you expect? This was just supposed to bridge the gap between t</span>
  <span id="freeText265050031013342532" style="display:none"><b><br>ACOBAR - A Court of Boredom and Repetition</b><br><br>Yep, that’s what I’m going with.<br><br>2.5 stars<br><br>This was...painful. Painful, because I’ve been SO obsessed with this series and beyond excited for this novella and somehow I just ended up feeling immensely bored and underwhelmed. Sure, seeing those characters again was nice and there were some cute scenes but half of what happened in this book was a repetition of past events. You might say, what did you expect? This was just supposed to bridge the gap between the old and the new series and it’s only a novella, but I still expected more. Mostly more plot.<br><br>Had I read this shortly after finishing book 3, I probably would’ve devoured this. You know, when I was still at that desperate point where I would’ve done almost anything to see more of those characters. Now, though? Not so much. <br><br>The only characters who didn’t annoy me were Rhys, Cassian, Az and Amren, but even they kinda bored me.<br><br>I’ve always struggled with Nesta but in this one her nasty attitude was just too fucking much. And whenever Elaine blinked her stupid doe eyes, I just wanted to shake and/or punch her. <br><br>I was also reminded that I really don’t like Feyre all that much.<br><br>And Mor...I don’t even know what to say about her. I used to love her but now I’m just indifferent.<br><br>Tamlin was pathetic! I’m really not his biggest fan but come on, give the guy a break.<br><br>Overall this book kinda bummed me out with so many depressed, unhappy and pathetic characters. If I’m going to read the new series then only because of Az and Cassian because I love these guys. It will be tough, though, since I don’t know how I’ll stomach any more Nesta.<br><br>And thanks for reminding me why I usually don’t bother with novellas.<br><br>Buddy read with my Belgian truffle. And yes, Kim, this is supposed to remind you of something! ;)<br><br>******************<br>FANGIRL MODE ACTIVATED IN 3...2...1...<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1524691466ra/25433429.gif" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>ONLY A FEW MORE DAAAAAAYS!!!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1524691466ra/25433430.gif" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>I apologize in advance for my upcoming behavior. Don't judge me too harshly please ;)<br><br>********************************<br>I’d pretty much sell my soul for more Rhysand.</span>

<div id="review_2093538890" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2093538890" />
    <a title="Beth" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44125660-beth"><img alt="Beth" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600268807p2/44125660.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2093538890?book_show_action=true">Aug 15, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Beth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Beth" href="/user/show/44125660-beth">Beth</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44125660-beth?shelf=2018-reads">2018-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44125660-beth?shelf=novella">novella</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44125660-beth?shelf=3-stars">3-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44125660-beth?shelf=nice-enough">nice-enough</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2093538890" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17281857157295480746"><b>3.5 Stars</b><br/><br/>I don't really know what to say about this? Did I love it? <i>No</i>. Did I like it? <i>yes...</i> it's just difficult, because I knew coming into this that it was a Novella, but I kind of expected more. For the first 50% it was okay, I felt slightly bored by it at the same time. <br/><br/>We see how the group are dealing with things after the war, and what may come in future books and what they're planning. But like I said, I was bored. Some parts made me go really, and then eye roll so much. I just think tha</span>
  <span id="freeText17281857157295480746" style="display:none"><b>3.5 Stars</b><br /><br />I don't really know what to say about this? Did I love it? <i>No</i>. Did I like it? <i>yes...</i> it's just difficult, because I knew coming into this that it was a Novella, but I kind of expected more. For the first 50% it was okay, I felt slightly bored by it at the same time. <br /><br />We see how the group are dealing with things after the war, and what may come in future books and what they're planning. But like I said, I was bored. Some parts made me go really, and then eye roll so much. I just think that it's coming across and trying to be a bit too perfect.<br /><br />However after saying that, there were indeed some really lovely moments and some things that I honestly really did just enjoy, so here are a few:<br />- We got a <b>Cassian</b> POV, he's one of my favourite characters in this series (alongside my queen that is Nesta)<br />- Women training!<br />- Talk about periods... that shit was relatable!<br />- I <u>loved</u> all things related to drunk decorating<br />- Toilet Situations + Amren :')<br />- Snowball fights<br />- That cake legit hurt my heart<br />- Solistice and all of the gifts, it was just so nice and I dunno it felt like a family coming together on a holiday and just being normal and there for each other, it was just too damn cute!<br />- All forms of Nessian interaction, my heart and soul needed it!<br />- The dresses!<br /><br />Now the things that I'm in a bit of a tizz over. Firstly I'm just going to address the elephant in the room, and that is <b>Nesta.</b> She's completely pulled away from everyone and is living in what can only be described as a depression. I don't know how to word this properly, but I'll try. It seemed to me that Nesta is struggling with a lot, and doesn't know how to deal with it. She's clearly not over her fathers death, she's coming to terms with becoming fae and seeing her sister go through that and has a lot of shit going on. HOWEVER, for me it seemed that a lot of the characters were kind of <i>judging</i> her, but when Feyre went through something similar it was kind of seen differently and she wasn't looked at to be a villain? I felt so sorry for Nesta, because in her dark time it seems as though no one seems to understand other than maybe Cassian. I hope we see her in the next book begin to progress and hopefully with time she will be able to heal and let someone *cough* Cassian *cough in to be able to actually talk to things about.<br /><br />Then we have Lucien, all I want for him is some form of happiness. I am so <b>pissed</b> at how he was treated in this book. One chapter. <b>ONE</b>. In that chapter he isn't treated the best, and honestly it just hurts my little heart. I'm literally rooting for him to have some form of happiness. HE NEEDS IT! While on the topic of Lucien, I may as well mention <i>Tamlin</i> this is also pretty difficult to explain. Before anyone comes preaching to me, I 1000000000% do <u>not</u> condone/agree with what he did in anyway shape or form. HOWEVER I did feel ever so slightly sorry for him, yes he's a dick, however he's literally lost everything and it was kind of sad to see this.<br /><br />Finally... as for the snippet extra chapters, I am ridiculously excited. We're going to have so much Nessian and I could cry with happiness, although I'm low key mad at what happened because yanno... where's the support?! Mixed feelings to say the least. I think I'm going to like the second book in the Novella more than this one, however it was nice enough.<br /><br />P.S - They mentioned the point. <b>I was living.</b><br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1493562550?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">A Court of Thorns and Roses</a> - 4 Stars<br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1564673810?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">A Court of Mist and Fury</a> - 5 Stars<br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1736956658?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">A Court of Wings and Ruin</a> - 4 Stars<br /><br />A Court of Frost and Starlight - 3.5 Stars<br /><br />------------<br />OH MY!!<br />We get a novella of the aftermath AND it's in Feyre and Rhysands POV?!<br /><br />Please for all of our sakes let Rhysand have more than two chapters.<br /><br />The excitement is REAL!<br />————— <br />25.11.17<br /><b>A Court of Frost and Starlight</b><br />We have a title!!!!!<br />Dear 2018, plz hurry much love all ACOTAR fans xoxoxo<br />—————<br />30.01.18<br />We have a cover! I’m<br />Not mad at it either and I actually prefer the UK cover... <b>ITS A MIRACLE</b><br />————-</span>
  <a data-text-id="17281857157295480746" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12402009-alana?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>,
